The Effect of Conjunction on Combined Divorce Delegation
Rulings when an outsider is given both 'amr bi yadik' and a direct divorce command

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the legal outcomes when an outsider is given both 'amr bi yadik' and an explicit divorce command, based on the conjunction used and the nature of the second command.

Core Idea
Fa links cause and effect (one divorce); waw separates commands, potentially yielding two divorces.

When a husband delegates authority to an outsider, the precise wording—especially the conjunction between the delegation and the divorce command—determines the legal outcome. This passage from al-Khaniyyah, cited in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, unpacks multiple scenarios based on whether the commands are joined with 'fa' (then) or 'waw' (and). Understanding these nuances is crucial for correctly applying Hanafi rulings on talaq and avoiding errors in counting divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two components
Every scenario combines 'amr bi yadik' (her affair is in your hand) with an explicit command to divorce (e.g., 'tallaqha'). Locate both in each variation.
The explicit command may appear first or second.
2
Classify the conjunction
Determine whether the commands are linked by 'fa' (cause-effect) or 'waw' (coordination). This determines whether one or both commands are operative.
The passage explicitly contrasts fa and waw for this purpose.
3
Identify the nature of the second command
Is the second command a delegation (tafweed) limited to the sitting, or an agency (tawkeel) that continues? Look for phrases like 'ja'altu amra dhaalika ilayka' (delegation) or 'a-binha' (agency for irrevocability).
Delegation expires when the sitting ends; agency does not.
4
Apply the outcome for each variation
Using the passage, state the number of divorces (one or two) and whether they are revocable (raj'i) or irrevocable (ba'in) for each wording.
Also note the exception: if husband intends three, three occur.
5
Summarize the broad distinction
The key difference is between fa (cause→effect, limits to one divorce) and waw (independent commands, can lead to two divorces if in the sitting). Delegation vs agency also affects timing and revocability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : إذا جمع لأجنبي بين الأمر باليد والأمر بالتطليق فما المعتبر منهما؟ قلت قال في الخانية : لو قال لغيره أمر امرأتي بيدك فطلقها فقال لها المأمور أنت طالق أو قال طلقتك يقع تطليقة بائنة إلا إذا نوى الزوج ثلاثاً فثلاث، وكذا لو قال طلقها فأمرها بيدك بخلاف ما لو قال أمرها بيدك في تطليقة أو بتطليقة فطلقها فطلقها المأمور في المجلس وقعت واحدة رجعية، ولو قال طلقها وقد جعلت أمر ذلك إليك فهو تفويض يقتصر على المجلس ويقع واحدة رجعية، ولو قال طلقها وقد جعلت إليك طلاقها فطلقها يقتصر على المجلس ويكون رجعياً. ولو قال طلقها فأبنها أو أبنها فطلقها فهو توكيل لا يقتصر على المجلس وللزوج الرجوع ويقع بائنة، وليس له أن يوقع أكثر من واحدة ولو قال طلقها وقد جعلت أمرها بيدك أو جعلت أمرها بيدك وطلقها كان الثاني غير الأول لأن الواو للعطف، فأما حرف الفاء في هذه المواضع يكون لبيان السبب فلا يملك إلا واحدة وإذا ذكر بحرف الواو فطلقها الوكيل في المجلس تبين بتطليقتين لأن الواقع بحكم الأمر يكون بائناً، فإذا كان أحدهما بائناً كان الآخر بائناً، فإن طلقها الوكيل بعد القيام عن المجلس تقع رجعية لأن التفويض يبطل بالقيام عن المجلس وبقي التوكيل بصريح الطلاق، وكذا لو قال أمرها بيدك وطلقها. ولو قال طلقها وأبنها أو قال أبنها وطلقها وطلقها في المجلس أو غيره يقع تطليقتان لأنه وكله بالإبانة والطلاق والتوكيل لا يبطل بالقيام عن المجلس فيقع طلاقان اهـ .
If you say: When an outsider is given both the command by hand and the command to divorce, which one is considered? I say: He said in al-Khaniyyah: If he said to another 'Your wife's affair is in your hand, so divorce her,' and the commanded one said to her 'You are divorced' or 'I divorced you,' one irrevocable divorce occurs unless the husband intended three, then three. And likewise if he said 'Divorce her so her affair is in your hand' contrary to if he said 'Her affair is in your hand for one divorce' or 'by one divorce' and he divorced her, and the commanded divorced her in the sitting, one revocable divorce occurs. And if he said 'Divorce her and I have placed her affair to you,' it is delegation limited to the sitting and one revocable divorce occurs. And if he said 'Divorce her and I have placed to you her divorce,' and he divorced her, it is limited to the sitting and is revocable. And if he said 'Divorce her and make her ba'in' or 'make her ba'in and divorce her,' it is agency not limited to the sitting, the husband has the right to revoke, and it occurs ba'in, and he cannot effect more than one. And if he said 'Divorce her and I have placed her affair in your hand' or 'I have placed her affair in your hand and divorce her,' the second is different from the first because the waw is for conjunction. As for the letter fa in these contexts, it is for explaining the cause, so he only owns one. And if mentioned with the letter waw, and the agent divorced her in the sitting, she becomes ba'in with two divorces because what occurs by virtue of the command is ba'in, so if one is ba'in, the other is also ba'in. If the agent divorced her after leaving the sitting, it occurs revocable because the delegation becomes void by leaving the sitting, and the agency for explicit divorce remains. And likewise if he said 'Her affair is in your hand and divorce her.' And if he said 'Divorce her and make her ba'in' or 'make her ba'in and divorce her,' and he divorced her in the sitting or elsewhere, two divorces occur because he appointed him for irrevocability and divorce, and agency does not become void by leaving the sitting, so two divorces occur.
Source pages p. 572

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical question: when an outsider (not the husband) is given both the general authority ('amr bi yadik') and a specific command to divorce, which governs? The answer from al-Khaniyyah details scenarios based on the wording and conjunction. First, if the husband says 'Your wife's affair is in your hand, so divorce her' (using faa), the delegate acts under 'amr bi yadik' first, resulting in one ba'in divorce (unless three intended). If he says 'Divorce her so her affair is in your hand' (faa), the divorce command comes first, and the 'amr bi yadik' is secondary, leading to one raj'i divorce if done in the sitting. If he says 'Her affair is in your hand for one divorce' (without conjunction), it is a limited delegation resulting in one raj'i. If he says 'Divorce her and I have placed her affair to you' (with waw), it is delegation limited to sitting, one raj'i. If he says 'Divorce her and make her ba'in' (waw), it is agency (not delegation) so not limited to sitting, results in one ba'in, and husband can revoke. The key distinction is between faa and waw: faa links the two as cause and effect, so only one action is intended; waw separates them, allowing both to operate independently. When 'amr bi yadik' and 'divorce' are combined with waw, the delegate can issue two divorces (one ba'in from the 'amr bi yadik' and one ba'in from the explicit command) if done in the sitting. After leaving the sitting, the delegation part is void, leaving only the agency for explicit divorce, so only one revocable divorce occurs. If he says 'Divorce her and make her ba'in' with waw, it remains agency for both, so two divorces occur regardless of location.

Key Terms
فاء (faa): The letter fa; it indicates cause-and-effect sequence, so the second action is a consequence of the first, limiting the delegate to one divorce.
واو (waw): The letter waw; it indicates conjunction, making both commands independent, allowing the delegate to act on both, potentially resulting in two divorces.
إبانة (ibaanah): Making a divorce irrevocable (ba'in); the delegate is authorized to give a ba'in divorce.
تفويض (tafweed): Delegation of authority; here it is contrasted with tawkeel; tafweed is limited to the sitting and results in raj'i divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband tells an outsider 'Your wife's affair is in your hand and divorce her' (using waw), and the outsider divorces her in the sitting, what is the result?
A) One revocable divorce.
B) One irrevocable divorce.
C) Two irrevocable divorces.
D) No divorce occurs because the wording is contradictory.

Key Takeaway
The conjunction 'fa' limits to one divorce as cause-and-effect; 'waw' allows two independent ba'in divorces when both commands are combined and the agent acts in the sitting.

Distinguishing Tamlik and Tawkil in Divorce Delegation
Definition and expansion of the tamlik/tawkil distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tamlik and tawkil in divorce delegation by identifying the four differentiating rulings and applying them to new cases.

Core Idea
Tamlik is ownership-based delegation restricted to the session; tawkil is agency-based delegation that extends beyond.

Delegating divorce to a third party (tafwid) is a nuanced area where the exact wording determines the legal nature. The Hanafi school distinguishes between tamlik (making the delegate an 'owner' of the divorce) and tawkil (simple agency). This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the critical differences, including how conjunctions like 'fa' and 'wa' reshape the delegation, and how the delegate's sanity affects validity. Understanding these distinctions prevents errors that could invalidate a divorce or lead to unintended consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Types of Delegation
Recognize that the author defines tamlik (تمليك) and tawkil (توكيل) as two distinct legal constructs. Tamlik gives the delegate authority as if he owns the divorce, while tawkil makes him an agent acting on the husband's behalf.
The term 'tamlik' is unique to Hanafi divorce law.
2
Analyze the Wording Clues
Study the phrases used: 'amruha biyadik' (her command is in your hand) often indicates tamlik; 'talkha' or 'abbinhā' (divorce her, separate her) indicates tawkil. Note how the conjunctions 'fa' (ف) and 'wa' (و) alter the nature: 'fa' usually combines into one delegation (tamlik or one agency), while 'wa' creates two separate delegations.
The passage provides many examples of wording and their consequences.
3
Memorize the Four Rulings of Difference
Extract the four points: (1) Session restriction – tamlik binds to the session (majlis), tawkil does not. (2) Revocability – tamlik cannot be revoked by the husband, tawkil can. (3) Dismissal of delegate – in tamlik the delegate cannot be dismissed, in tawkil he can. (4) Effect of husband’s insanity – tamlik is not invalidated by the husband’s insanity, tawkil is.
These are the core operational rules.
4
Examine the Case of a Minor or Insane Delegate
Consider the disagreement: al-Muhit validates delegation to a minor/insane person as tamlik because it contains an implied suspension (ta'liq) – the divorce occurs if the delegate speaks, even if he does not understand. Al-Khaniyya and Muhammad require the delegate to be capable of expression at the time of utterance. The relied-upon position distinguishes initial delegation (valid if the delegate can speak) from later insanity (divorce invalid if he does not understand).
This illustrates how ta'liq (conditional suspension) overrides the usual requirement of sanity.
5
Apply the Principles to New Scenarios
Given a husband's exact wording, determine whether it is tamlik or tawkil, then predict the effect on the session, revocability, number of divorces, and validity if the delegate is a child or insane person.
Practice with examples such as 'Your command is in your hand and divorce her' (wa) vs 'Your command is in your hand, so divorce her' (fa).

Source Text

كتاب الطلاق فصل في المشيئة

الهداية والبيع لا يحتمل ظاهر في أنه لا يحتمل التعليق بالمشيئة، وإذا لم يحتمله فهل يبطل أو يصح ويبطل التعليق؟ قال في المحيط من كتاب الأيمان من قسم التعليق : لو قال لرجل بعت عبدي منك بكذا إن شئت فقبل يكون بيعاً صحيحاً إذ البيع لا يحتمل التعليق اهـ. قيد بقوله «طلقها» لأنه لو قال أمر امرأتي بيدك يقتصر على المجلس ولا يملك الرجوع على الأسح وإن قال بعض هذا توكيل لأنه صرح بالأمر كذا في الخلاصة. وكذا لو قال جعلت إليك طلاقها فطلقها يقتصر على المجلس ويكون رجعياً. كذا في الخانية. وفي الظهيرية: لو قال قل لامرأتي أمرك بيدك لا يصير الأمر بيدها ما لم يقل المأمور بخلاف قل لها إن أمرها بيدها. ولو قال أمرها بيد الله وبيدك انفرد المخاطب وذكر الله هنا للتبرك عرفاً، وكذا في العتاق والبيع والإجارة والخلع والطلاق على مال ولو قال أمرها بيدي ويدك لا ينفرد المخاطب، ولو قال طلقها ما شاء الله وشئت فطلقها المخاطب لا يقع لاستعماله للاستثناء، ولو قال طلقها بما شاء الله وشئت من المال فطلقها المخاطب جاز لأن المشيئة هنا تنصرف إلى البدل لا إلى التفويض اهـ. فإن قلت : إذا جمع لأجنبي بين الأمر باليد والأمر بالتطليق فما لو قال أمرها بيدك في تطليقة أو بتطليقة فطلقها فطلقها المأمور في المجلس وقعت واحدة رجعية، ولو قال طلقها وقد جعلت أمر ذلك إليك فهو تفويض يقتصر على المجلس ويقع واحدة رجعية، ولو قال طلقها وقد جعلت إليك يعتبر به ا.هـ. ولا يخفى ما فيه فإن المعلق بالمشيئة على كلام المتعقب إنما هو الوكالة لا البيع، وعلى هذا فما معنى قوله لاتصافه بها قبل مشيئة البيع قوله : ( فيحتاج إلى الفرق أقول : لعل الفرق ما مر من أنه تمليك .

الجنون ونظيره ما ذكره في الخانية بعده : لو وكل رجلاً ببيع عبده فجن الوكيل جنوناً يعقل فيه البيع والشراء ثم باع الوكيل لا ينعقد بيعه، ولو وكل رجلاً مجنوناً بهذه الصفة . ببيع عبده ثم باع الوكيل نفذ بیعه فيه على الموكل فإذا أتى بذلك نفذ بيعه على الموكل اهـ. وفي تفويض ببيع الطلاق وإن كان لا عهدة أصلاً ولكن الزوج حين التفويض لم يعلق إلا على كلام عاقل، فإذا طلق وهو مجنون لم يوجد الشرط بخلاف ما إذا فوض إلى مجنون ابتداء وبين التفويض إلى مجنون وتوكيله بالبيع فرق فإنه في التفويض يصح وإن لم يعقل أصلاً باعتبار معنى التعليق، نفذ وكل
Book of Divorce, Chapter on Conditional Wishes. Al-Hidayah: The sale does not accept a condition in appearance, so it does not accept suspension upon a wish. If it does not accept it, is it invalid or does it become valid and the suspension is invalid? He said in al-Muhit from the book of Oaths from the section on suspension: If a man said to another, 'I have sold my slave to you for such-and-such if you wish,' and he accepts, the sale is valid because the sale does not accept suspension. He restricted it by his saying 'divorce her' because if he says 'your command is in your hand concerning my wife,' it is restricted to the session and he does not have the right to revoke, but if he said some of this, it is agency because he explicitly commanded. Similarly, if he said 'I have placed the divorce of her in your hand,' then he divorces her, it is restricted to the session and is a revocable divorce. Similar in al-Khaniyya. In al-Dhahiriya: If he said 'Say to my wife: your command is in your hand,' it does not become in her hand as long as the commanded one does not say it, unlike 'Say to her: her command is in her hand.' And if he said 'Her command is in the hand of Allah and your hand,' the addressee is singled out, and mentioning Allah here is for blessing customarily; similar in manumission, sale, hire, khul', and divorce for compensation. And if he said 'Her command is in my hand and your hand,' the addressee is not singled out. And if he said 'Divorce her as Allah wills and as you will,' then the addressee divorces her, it does not occur due to using it as an exception. And if he said 'Divorce her for whatever Allah wills and you will of compensation,' then the addressee divorces her, it is permissible because the wish here refers to the substitute, not the delegation. If you say: When he combines for a stranger the command of the hand and the command of divorce, which of them is considered? I say: In al-Khaniyya: If he said to another 'Your command is in your hand concerning my wife, so divorce her,' and the commanded one says to her 'You are divorced' or 'I have divorced you,' one irrevocable divorce occurs unless the husband intended three, then three. Similarly if he said 'Divorce her, and your command in your hand concerning her' unlike if he said 'Your command is in your hand concerning one divorce' and then he said 'Divorce her,' so the commanded one divorces her in the session, one revocable divorce occurs. And if he said 'Divorce her, and I have placed that affair to you,' it is delegation restricted to the session and one revocable divorce occurs. And if he said 'Divorce her, and I have placed the divorce of her to you,' so he divorces her, it is restricted to the session and is revocable. And if he said 'Divorce her and make her irrevocable' or 'make her irrevocable and divorce her,' it is agency not restricted to the session, the husband has the right to revoke, and it occurs irrevocably, and he is not allowed to effect more than one. And if he said 'Divorce her, and I have placed her command in your hand' or 'I have placed her command in your hand and divorce her,' the second is different from the first because the waw is for conjunction. As for the letter fa in these contexts, it is for explaining the cause, so he does not own except one. And if it is mentioned with the waw, then the agent divorces her in the session, she becomes separated by two divorces because that which occurs by virtue of the command is irrevocable; if one of them is irrevocable, the other is irrevocable. And if the agent divorces her after leaving the session, it occurs as revocable because the delegation is nullified by leaving the session, and the agency with explicit divorce remains. Similarly if he said 'Your command is in your hand concerning her and divorce her.' And if he said 'Divorce her and make her irrevocable' or 'make her irrevocable and divorce her' and he divorces her in the session or otherwise, two divorces occur because he appointed him as agent for making irrevocable and divorce, and agency is not nullified by leaving the session, so two divorces occur. ... It is considered thereby. It is not hidden what is in it, for the suspended upon a wish according to the speech of the critic is only the agency, not the sale; upon this, what is the meaning of his saying 'because of its being described with it before the wish of sale'? He says: 'So it needs a distinction. I say: Perhaps the distinction is what passed, that it is tamlik.' The summary: When he combines for a stranger the command of the hand and the command of divorce with fa, it is one entity and the command of the hand is not considered, whether it comes first or later; thus it is restricted to the session and he does not have the right to dismiss him, and it occurs irrevocably. If it is with waw, then they are two delegations: the command of the hand is tamlik which takes its rulings, and the command of divorce is agency which takes its rulings. If he commands him with making irrevocable and divorce with fa, it is one agency; if with waw, it is agency for making irrevocable and divorce, so two divorces occur. And if he combines between the making to him and the command of divorce, if he precedes the making, it is tamlik; if he delays it, it is agency. The apparent is that there is no difference between fa and waw. Up to here, the difference between tamlik and agency has become clear in four rulings: tamlik is restricted to the session, and it is not valid to revoke it, nor to dismiss him, and it is not invalidated by the insanity of the husband. These rulings are reversed in agency. If the author had said 'and if he says to other than her, divorce her' it would have been better to include when he commands his wife to divorce her co-wife as we have presented. It will come from al-Khaniyya in the chapter on suspension that if he said 'every woman I marry, I have sold her divorce to you for a dirham,' then he marries a woman, and the woman who was with him says when she learns of the marriage to another, 'I accept' or 'I have divorced her' or 'I have purchased her divorce,' the one he married is divorced; but if the one with him says before he marries another, 'I accept,' her acceptance is not valid because it is acceptance before the offer. He said: 'The man is general, so it includes when he delegates to a minor who does not understand or an insane person.' Thus in al-Muhit: If he places her command in the hand of a minor who does not understand or an insane person, that is in his authority as long as he is in the session because this is tamlik that includes a suspension in it; if it is not valid from the perspective of tamlik, it is valid from the perspective of the meaning of suspension, so we deemed it valid from the perspective of suspension, as if he said 'if the insane person says to you, you are divorced, you are divorced,' and from the perspective of the meaning of tamlik, it is restricted to the session, acting on both aspects. But in al-Khaniyya: He said, 'A man delegated the divorce of his wife to...' He said in al-Asl: 'If he is one who expresses, it is permissible.' Its implication is that if he does not, it is not permissible. There is a difference between what is in al-Muhit and what is in it because the minor who does not understand requires that he be one who speaks in order for the divorce to occur upon her, and expression does not necessarily imply understanding, as is not hidden. In al-Khaniyya: If the one made to be in charge (maj‘ul ilayhi) becomes insane after the delegation and then divorces, Muhammad said: If he does not understand what he says, his divorce does not occur. Thus, according to this, there is a distinction between delegating to an insane person initially and the occurrence of insanity afterwards. Its analogy is what he mentioned in al-Khaniyya after it: If a man appoints another as agent to sell his slave, then the agent becomes insane with an insanity in which he understands buying and selling, then the agent sells, his sale is not enforceable. And if a man appoints an insane person of this description as agent to sell his slave, then the agent sells, his sale is enforceable because if he was not insane at the time of agency, the liability (ʿuhda) in the sale is upon the agent. After the agent becomes insane, if he sells, the liability is upon the principal, so it is not enforceable. As for when the agent is insane at the time of agency, the liability is upon the principal, so if he performs it, his sale is enforceable upon the principal. And in delegating the divorce of a sale, although there is no liability at all, but the husband at the time of delegation did not suspend except upon the speech of a sane person; so if he divorces while insane, the condition is not found, unlike when he delegates to an insane person initially. And there is a difference between delegation to an insane person and his agency for sale: in delegation, it is valid even if he does not understand at all, due to the consideration of the meaning of suspension. It is enforced. (End)
Source pages p. 573

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explains the rulings of delegating divorce (tafwid al-talaq) to a third party. It distinguishes between two types of delegation: tamlik (تمليك) and tawkil (توكيل). Tamlik is when the husband gives the authority to the delegate to effect divorce at his discretion, but it is restricted to the session (majlis) and cannot be revoked or dismissed. Tawkil is simple agency where the delegate acts on the husband's behalf; it is not restricted to the session, and the husband may revoke it. The passage examines various phrases that indicate whether the delegation is tamlik or tawkil, especially the use of conjunctions 'fa' (ف) and 'wa' (و). 'Fa' typically indicates a single act of delegation (tamlik or tawkil depending on context), while 'wa' indicates two separate delegations. Four specific differences are highlighted: (1) tamlik restricts to the session; tawkil does not. (2) tamlik cannot be revoked; tawkil can. (3) in tamlik, the delegate cannot be dismissed; in tawkil, he can. (4) tamlik is not invalidated by the husband's insanity; tawkil is. The passage also addresses cases where the delegate is a minor or insane person: delegation to such a person is valid as a kind of suspended tamlik, considered effective based on the meaning of suspension (ta'liq), even if the delegate does not understand, as long as the words are spoken. However, if the delegate becomes insane after delegation, the divorce is not effective because the condition (sanity at the time of utterance) is not met. A useful analogy is drawn with agency for sale, where liability (ʿuhda) determines validity. The overarching principle is that the husband's intention and the wording used determine the legal nature of the delegation.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): A form of delegation in divorce where the husband grants the delegate authority to effect divorce at his discretion, restricted to the session and irrevocable.
توكيل (tawkil): Agency in divorce where the delegate acts on the husband's behalf; not restricted to the session and revocable.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of an effect (divorce) upon a condition (e.g., the delegate's utterance).
العهدة (al-ʿuhda): Liability or responsibility, especially concerning the validity of a sale by an agent.
المجلس (al-majlis): The session where the delegation occurs; some types of delegation are restricted to this session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes tamlik (تمليك) from tawkil (توكيل) in the delegation of divorce?
A) Tamlik is restricted to the session and cannot be revoked; tawkil is not restricted and can be revoked.
B) Tamlik requires a witness; tawkil does not.
C) Tamlik can only be done with a minor; tawkil only with an adult.
D) Tamlik results in three divorces; tawkil results in one.

Key Takeaway
Tamlik in divorce delegation is an ownership-based authority restricted to the session and irrevocable, while tawkil is an agency that continues beyond the session and is revocable—the wording of the delegation determines which applies.

Delegation of Divorce to a Minor or Insane Person
Ruling on invalidity of delegation to minor/insane, compared to agency in sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why delegation of divorce to a minor or insane person is invalid in the Hanafi school and explain the comparison with agency in sale.

Core Idea
Delegation of divorce requires the delegate to understand the action; a minor or insane person lacks capacity.

This passage clarifies a key condition for valid delegation (tafweed) of divorce: the delegate must possess intellect and comprehension. The author compares this to agency (tawkeel) in sale, where understanding is similarly required. The ruling highlights a departure from the general fiqhi principle that allows more leniency in continuation than in initiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Locate the statement that delegation to a minor or insane person is invalid. Note the condition: the delegate must 'understand sale and purchase' (in the analogy of agency). This indicates the underlying requirement of 'aql (intellect).
The ruling is fasid (invalid) due to lack of capacity.
2
Analyze the comparative proof (qiyas)
The author draws an analogy between delegation in divorce and agency in sale. In both, the agent/delegate must understand the nature of the transaction. Since a minor/insane person cannot understand, the delegation is invalid by qiyas.
The qiyas is based on the common illa: need for comprehension in a legally significant act.
3
Contrast with the general fiqhi principle
The passage notes a reversal of the usual principle 'leniency in continuance, not in initiation' (yatasamah fi al-baqa' ma la yatasamah fi al-ibtida'). Here, in the sub-branches of delegation and agency, the opposite applies: initiation is allowed more leniency (e.g., appointing a discerning minor as agent in sale may be valid if he understands) but continuance is not (e.g., if the agent loses capacity later, the delegation ends).
This exception is specific to these cases; the general principle holds elsewhere.
4
Extract the practical implication
The mufta bihi ruling: delegation of divorce to a minor or insane person is invalid. The husband must either divorce himself or appoint a sane, understanding adult.
This protects the sanctity of marriage by ensuring deliberate, informed action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق فصل في المشيئة
وفي التوكيل بالبيع لا يصح إلا إذا كان يعقل البيع والشراء كما قيده به في الخانية وكأنه بمعنى المعتوه ومن فرعي التفويض والتوكيل بالبيع ظهر أنه تسومح في الابتداء ما لم يتسامح في البقاء وهو خلاف القاعدة الفقهية من أنه يتسامح في البقاء ما لا يتسامح في الابتداء.
Book of Divorce, Chapter on Conditional Will. And regarding agency in sale, it is not valid except if [the agent] understands sale and purchase, as it is restricted in al-Khaniyah; it is as if it means the feeble-minded. And from the two sub-branches of delegation and agency in sale, it appears that leniency is given in initiation that is not given in continuance, contrary to the fiqhi principle that leniency is given in continuance that is not given in initiation.
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the validity of delegation (tafweed) and agency (tawkeel) in divorce. The author clarifies that for agency in sale, the agent must understand the transaction; the same applies to the delegate in divorce: a minor or insane person cannot be delegated because they lack comprehension. This is contrasted with the general fiqhi principle that typically allows more leniency in continuation (bagha’) than in initiation (ibtida’), but here the opposite is observed in the sub-branches of delegation and agency in sale.

Key Terms
التفويض (at-tafweed): Delegation of authority in divorce, where the husband gives the wife or another the power to divorce.
التوكيل (at-tawkeel): Agency; appointing someone to act on one's behalf, here in divorce or sale.
المعتوه (al-ma‘tooh): A person of weak intellect or feeble-minded, similar to an insane person in lacking legal capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Joint Agents in Divorce: Combined Action Fulfills Command
Ruling on joint agents in divorce; combined actions fulfill total command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on joint agents in divorce and apply it to scenarios where agents act individually or in combination.

Core Idea
Joint agents in divorce cannot act alone, but their combined actions fulfill a total-number command.

When a husband appoints two agents to divorce his wife, neither agent may act independently; they must act together. However, if the husband commands them to effect a specific number of divorces (e.g., three), and each agent pronounces a partial number, their actions combine to produce the total. This ruling highlights the principle that joint agency requires consensus, but the intended outcome can be achieved through cumulative effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agency arrangement
The husband placed the matter of divorce in the hands of two men jointly. This means the authority is shared; neither can act alone. First, confirm that the agents are co-agents (wakeelan) with equal authority.
Joint agency is distinct from separate agency where each can act independently.
2
Parse the husband's command
The husband said 'Divorce my wife three times.' This is a command for a specific total number, not a command for each to pronounce three. The agents must collectively realize the number.
The command is a single imperative to both.
3
Analyze the agents' actions
One agent pronounced one divorce, the other pronounced two. Individually, neither performed the full command. But because the command was for a total of three, the combined actions equal the commanded number.
The ruling does not require each agent to pronounce the full number.
4
Determine the legal effect
The passage states 'she is divorced three times.' The divorce is valid (sahih) and counts as three. The joint agency does not block the cumulative effect when the command is for a specific total.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة: لو جعل أمرها بيد رجلين لا ينفرد أحدهما، ولو قال لهما طلقا امرأتي ثلاثاً فطلقها أحدهما واحدة والآخر ثنتين طلقت ثلاثاً .اهـ.
And in al-Khulasa: If he placed her matter in the hands of two men, neither of them acts individually. And if he said to them, 'Divorce my wife three times,' and one divorced her once and the other twice, she is divorced three times.
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage from al-Khulasa states a ruling: when a husband delegates the authority to divorce to two persons jointly, neither can act alone; they must act together. However, if the husband explicitly commands them to divorce a total of three times, and each performs a part (one gives one divorce, the other two), the total of three divorces takes effect, because their actions combine to fulfill the command. The joint agency does not prevent the combined effect when the command is for a specific number.

Key Terms
الوكيلان (al-wakeelan): Two agents appointed jointly; they have no independent authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) One, because only one agent spoke first
C) Two, because the second agent gave two

Key Takeaway
When two joint agents are commanded to effect a total number of divorces, their partial divorces combine to produce the commanded total.

Delegation via Messenger: The Effect of Wording
Ruling that sending delegation via a messenger is valid, and two similar wordings have different effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that delegation via messenger is valid and distinguish when the wife gains authority based on the wording used.

Core Idea
The precise wording of the delegation determines whether the wife's authority begins immediately or only after the messenger speaks.

In Hanafi law, a husband may delegate the power of divorce to his wife through a messenger. This lesson clarifies that such delegation is valid. More importantly, it reveals a subtle but legally significant distinction between two phrasings: one where the messenger is commanded to 'tell her' something, and another where the messenger is told to 'tell her that' something. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining the exact moment the wife acquires the right to divorce herself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of sending tafwid (delegation) via a messenger. The ruling is that it is valid (jāʾiz).
This is a ruling from al-Zahiriyyah.
2
Examine the two wordings
The passage presents two phrases: (1) 'Tell her: your matter is in your hand' (a direct command), and (2) 'Tell her that your matter is in your hand' (an indirect report).
3
Distinguish the legal effect
With the first phrasing, the delegation only takes effect when the messenger actually says the words to the wife. With the second, the delegation is effective immediately upon the wife hearing the message, regardless of the messenger's repetition.
The presence of 'inna' (that) changes the legal consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو أرسل التفويض إليها مع رجل فإنه يجوز بالأولى، وقدمنا قريباً عن الظهيرية الفرق بين قوله قل لها أمرك بيدك حيث لا يكون الأمر بيدها إلا إذا قال لها وقوله قل لها إن أمرك بيدك حيث يكون الأمر بيدها من غير قول الرسول.
And the author indicated that if he sent the delegation to her via a man, it is permissible a fortiori. And we presented recently from al-Zahiriyyah the difference between his saying 'Tell her: your matter is in your hand,' where her matter is not in her hand unless he (the messenger) says it to her, and his saying 'Tell her that your matter is in your hand,' where her matter is in her hand without the messenger's statement.
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling on sending divorce delegation through a messenger. The author notes that this is permissible, especially when the husband cannot directly communicate. The key distinction from al-Zahiriyyah is between two similar phrases: if the husband says to the messenger, 'Tell her: your matter is in your hand' (direct command), the delegation only takes effect when the messenger actually says those words to the wife. If he says, 'Tell her that your matter is in your hand' (indirect report), the delegation is effective immediately upon the wife hearing the report, without requiring the messenger to formally pronounce it. This distinction affects when the wife gains the right to divorce herself.

Key Terms
الرسول (ar-rasool): A messenger who conveys the husband's words to the wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The first is invalid; the second is valid
D) There is no difference

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the wording of delegation via messenger determines whether the wife's authority begins immediately or only after the messenger speaks.

Condition 'If She Wills' Restricts Agency to the Assembly
Ruling that adding 'if she wills' restricts agency to the assembly.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agency conditioned on the wife's will and explain why the agency is restricted to the assembly using qiyas.

Core Idea
An agency conditioned on the wife's will is valid only if she wills in the same assembly; leaving before divorce voids the agency.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq refines the ruling on agency (wikalah) in divorce when the husband adds the condition 'if she wills.' The central issue is whether the agent's authority continues after leaving the assembly where the wife expressed her will. The passage resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute by affirming the restriction to the assembly, based on an analogy with divorce itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its condition
The act is appointing an agent (wakil) for divorce with the added condition 'if she wishes.' Determine the ruling on the agency when the wife wills in the same assembly.
The condition is the wife's will (mashiyyah).
2
Trace the dalil (evidence) from al-Khaniyah
The passage cites al-Khaniyah: the agency is not effective until the wife wills in her assembly. This is because the condition ties the agency to her will, and her will itself is confined to the assembly.
The source is a well-known Hanafi text.
3
Understand the qiyas (analogy) used
The ruling is analogous to divorce conditioned on her will: if the husband says 'you are divorced if you wish,' the divorce only occurs if she wills in the same assembly. Similarly, the agency is restricted.
The asl is divorce, the far' is agency; the illa is that the will is restricted to the majlis.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf (dispute)
Some scholars argued that once the wife wills, the agency becomes unrestricted like an unconditional appointment. They claimed the condition is fulfilled, so the agency should not lapse upon leaving.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
The passage declares the book's answer (jawab al-kitab) as correct (sahih) because the agency is built on the wife's will, which is inherently restricted to the assembly.
The mufta bihi is the restriction; the agent must act before leaving.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال المؤلف إلا إذا زاد إن شئت أو شاءت» لكان أولى لأنه يتقيد بالمجلس إذا وجد أحدهما لما في الخانية : لو قال لغيره أنت وكيلي في طلاق امرأتي إن شاءت أو هويت أو أرادت لم يكن وكيلاً حتى تشاء المرأة في مجلسها لأنه علق التوكيل بمشيئتها فيقتصر على مجلس العلم كما لو علق الطلاق بمشيئتها، فإذا شاءت في المجلس يكون وكيلاً، فإن قام الوكيل عن المجلس قبل أن يطلق بطلت الوكالة. وقال بعض العلماء : لا تبطل لأن المعلق بالشرط عند وجود الشرط كالمرسل فيصير كأنه قال بعد مشيئتها أنت وكيلي في طلاقها فلا يقتصر على المجلس. قالوا: والصحيح جواب الكتاب لأن ثبوت الوكالة بالطلاق بناء على ما فوض إليها من المسيئة ومشيئتها تقتصر على المجلس فكذلك الوكالة اهـ.
And if the author had said 'except if he adds 'if you wish' or 'if she wishes,'' it would be better because it is restricted to the assembly when one of them occurs. This is based on what is in al-Khaniyah: If he said to another, 'You are my agent in divorcing my wife if she wishes or desires or intends,' he is not an agent until the woman wills in her assembly, because he conditioned the agency on her will, so it is confined to the assembly of knowledge, just as if he conditioned the divorce on her will. So if she wills in the assembly, he becomes an agent; if the agent leaves the assembly before divorcing, the agency is invalidated. And some scholars said: It is not invalidated because that which is conditioned on a condition, when the condition exists, is like an unrestricted statement, so it becomes as if he said after her will, 'You are my agent in her divorce,' so it is not restricted to the assembly. They said: The correct is the answer of the book because the establishment of agency in divorce is based on what was delegated to her of the will, and her will is restricted to the assembly, so likewise the agency.
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of adding a condition like 'if she wills' when appointing an agent for divorce. According to al-Khaniyah, the agency is contingent upon the wife expressing her will in the same assembly (majlis) where the husband made the statement. If the wife wills in that assembly, the agent becomes authorized, but if the agent leaves the assembly before divorcing, the agency is revoked. Some later scholars argue that once the condition is fulfilled, the agency becomes independent of the assembly, but the correct position (sahih) is the former—because the wife's will (mashiyyah) is itself restricted to the assembly, so the agency derived from it is also restricted. This is a critical refinement showing an intra-Hanafi dispute resolved in favor of the book's ruling.

Key Terms
المجلس (al-majlis): The assembly or session where the husband's statement and the wife's will occur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The agency continues
B) The agency is invalidated
C) The wife must will again
D) The husband must reappoint the agent

Key Takeaway
An agency conditioned on the wife's will is restricted to the assembly; the agent must act before leaving, or the agency expires.

Understanding Tawkeel in Divorce as Ta'liq and the Role of Sanity
Marginal commentary reconciling two rulings on tawkeel in divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the requirement of sanity at appointment vs execution in tawkeel in divorce, and apply the Hanafi rule that tawkeel is treated as ta'liq.

Core Idea
Tawkeel in divorce is a suspension (ta'liq), not a transfer of authority.

This marginal note from al-Bazzaziyyah clarifies a crucial point: when a husband appoints an agent to pronounce divorce, that appointment is not a standard agency but a conditional suspension. This distinction determines whether the agent must be sane when the divorce actually occurs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two points to reconcile
The note begins by referencing a previous statement requiring 'aql (intellect) for the validity of tawkeel, then cites al-Bazzaziyyah's statement that tawkeel in divorce is ta'liq and thus takes effect even if the agent is intoxicated. These two points seem contradictory: one requires sanity, the other says intoxication does not prevent effect.
Recognize that the contradiction is only apparent.
2
Understand ta'liq in this context
Ta'liq means the divorce is suspended upon a condition—here, the condition is the agent's pronouncement of the divorce formula. Once the agent says the formula, the divorce occurs automatically, traced back to the husband's appointment, not the agent's current state.
This is a distinctive Hanafi view: tawkeel is not a transfer of authority but a conditional delegation.
3
Explain why ta'liq makes sanity at execution irrelevant
Because the divorce is attributed to the husband's original appointment, the agent's mental state at the moment of pronouncement does not affect validity. The appointment itself was a valid contract requiring sanity; once valid, the suspended effect follows regardless of the agent's later capacity.
This is the key insight: the ruling from al-Bazzaziyyah addresses execution, not appointment.
4
Distinguish the requirement of sanity at appointment
The initial appointment (tawkeel) is a contract that requires the agent to be sane. If the agent is insane or a child at the time of appointment, the tawkeel itself is invalid. But once validly appointed, later intoxication does not nullify it.
Thus the two statements are consistent: sanity required at appointment, not at execution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فعلى هذا لا بد من التقييد بالعقل) تأمله مع ما يأتي أواخر هذه السوادة عن البزازية من قوله «التوكيل بالطلاق تعليق الطلاق بلفظ «الوكيل ولذا يقع منه حال سكره إلا أن يجاب بأن هذا لا ينافي اشتراط العقل لصحة التوكيل ابتداء .
His saying: ('Therefore it is necessary to restrict [the ruling] by intellect') — consider it with what comes at the end of this marginal note from al-Bazzaziyyah, his saying: 'Agency in divorce is a suspension (ta'liq) of divorce by the word 'agent,' and for that reason it takes effect from him even in a state of intoxication, unless it can be answered that this does not contradict the requirement of intellect for the validity of agency initially.'
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This is a marginal note (hashiya) refining the previous point about requiring intellect (aql) for the validity of tawkeel in divorce. The commentator points out that al-Bazzaziyyah states that tawkeel in divorce is actually a form of ta'liq (suspension) of divorce using the word 'agent,' which is why if the agent becomes intoxicated, the divorce still takes effect (because ta'liq does not require the agent's intellect at the moment of execution). However, this does not negate the requirement of intellect for the initial appointment of the agent (since the appointment is a contract that requires sanity). Thus, the agent must be sane when appointed, but if he later loses sanity temporarily, the divorce may still occur.

Key Terms
التعليق (at-ta'liq): Suspending a legal effect (here divorce) on a condition; once the condition is met, the effect occurs automatically.
التوكيل بالطلاق (at-tawkeel bi t-talāq): The act of a husband appointing an agent to pronounce divorce on his behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a divorce effected by an intoxicated agent still occur according to the marginal note?
A) Because intoxication does not affect divorce
B) Because the tawkeel is a ta'liq (suspension) of divorce, not requiring the agent's intellect at execution
C) Because the agent was sane when appointed
D) Because the husband is responsible for the divorce

Key Takeaway
Tawkeel in divorce is treated as ta'liq, so the agent must be sane at appointment but not at execution.

Requirement of the Wife's Will in Divorce Agency
Establishing the rule of wife's will and husband's council in agency for divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the wife's will must be expressed in her council for a valid agency in divorce and distinguish between tawkīl and tamlīk in this context.

Core Idea
Agency in divorce requires the wife's will in her council; delay invalidates.

This lesson examines a nuanced Hanafi ruling on agency for divorce. The author from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that when a husband appoints an agent to divorce his wife conditional on her request, the wife must express her will in the council where she learns of the agency. A common pitfall is delaying the pronouncement, which voids the agency. Understanding this distinction prevents invalid divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Central Rule
State the two conditions for a valid agency in divorce: the wife's will in her council and the agent's pronouncement in his own council.
2
Distinguish Tamlīk from Tawkīl
Understand why the restriction to the council does not make it a transfer of ownership. The condition is on the wife's will, so it remains an agency.
This distinction affects the right to dismiss the agent.
3
Analyze the al-Qunyah Example
Work through the case: the wife delayed her request beyond the council of knowledge. Why does the divorce not occur?
The delay means her will was not in the proper council.
4
Extract the Practical Warning
Note the author's caution that most divorces by letter fail because agents delay after the wife's will. The lesson is to act immediately.
This is a common error among laypeople and agents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المشيئة يبيع الوكالة اهـ. وحاصله أنه لا بد من مشيئتها في مجلسها وتطليقه في مجلسه وهذا مما يلغز به فيقال : وكالة تقيدت بمجلس الوكيل وإياك أن تفهم من التقييد بالمجلس أنه تمليك لأن ذلك فيما إذا علقه بمشيئته وهنا علقه بمشيئتها فكان توكيلاً فيملك عزله. وفي القنية : كتب إلى أخيه : أما بعد فإن وصل إليك كتابي فطلق امرأتي إن سألت ذلك، فوصل وعرض عليها فلم تسأل الطلاق إلا بعد أربعة أيام أو خمسة ثم سألته فطلقها لا يقع. قال له طلق امرأتي إن يصير وكيلاً ما لم تشأ ولها المشيئة في مجلس علمها ، فإذا شاءت صار وكيلاً، فلو طلقها في المجلس يقع، ولو قام عن مجلسه بطل التوكيل. وينبغي أن يحفظ هذا فإن البلوى فيه تعم فإن عامة كتب الطلاق على هذه المثابة والوكلاء يؤخرون الإيقاع عن مشيئتها ولا يدرون أن الطلاق لا يقع .اهـ.
Chapter on Conditional Will. Selling of agency, etc. Its summary: It is necessary that her will [occurs] in her council and his divorce in his council. And this is a puzzle: an agency restricted to the agent's council. Do not understand from the restriction to the council that it is a transfer of ownership, because that is when he conditions it on his own will, but here he conditions it on her will, so it is an agency, so he has the right to dismiss him. In al-Qunyah: He wrote to his brother: 'To proceed: When my letter reaches you, divorce my wife if she asks for that.' It arrived and he presented it to her, but she did not ask for divorce except after four or five days, then she asked him and he divorced her; it does not occur. He said: 'Divorce my wife' makes him an agent as long as she does not will, and she has the will in the council of her knowledge; when she wills, he becomes an agent. If he divorces her in the council, it occurs; if he leaves his council, the agency is void. It is befitting to memorize this because calamity is widespread in it; indeed, most divorce letters are like this, and agents delay the execution after her will, not knowing that the divorce does not occur. End.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key principle in Hanafi law regarding agency in divorce. The author opens by distinguishing between tamlik (transfer of ownership) and tawkīl (agency). The apparent restriction to a council might be mistaken for tamlik, but here it is agency because the condition is attached to the wife's will, not the husband's. The example from al-Qunyah illustrates: a brother writes to his agent to divorce his wife if she asks; she asks after days, and the agent divorces her; the divorce does not occur because she must ask in the council of her knowledge (the council where she learns of the agency). The ruling underscores that the wife's will (mashi'ah) must be expressed in her council, and the agent must act in his own council. This is a common pitfall, as people often delay the divorce after the wife's will, invalidating it. The passage is practical, warning agents to execute promptly.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakālah): Agency; the act of authorizing someone to act on one's behalf
مشيئة (mashī'ah): Will or volition of the wife, which must be expressed in her council for the agency to activate
تمليك (tamlīk): Transfer of ownership; here distinguished from agency as a different legal construct

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example from al-Qunyah, why did the divorce not occur when the agent divorced the wife after she asked four days later?
A) Because the agent did not pronounce the divorce in the husband's council
B) Because the wife did not express her will in the council of her knowledge
C) Because the brother's letter was invalid
D) Because the wife changed her mind

Key Takeaway
The wife's will must be expressed in the council of her knowledge for a valid agency divorce; delay invalidates the divorce.

Ambiguous Expressions in Divorce Agency
Explaining rulings when agency is expressed through ambiguous phrases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which ambiguous expressions do not create agency for divorce and explain the underlying Hanafi principle.

Core Idea
Divorce agency requires explicit delegation; mere assent or non-prohibition is insufficient.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that divorce agency is a serious matter requiring clear words. A simple 'yes' to a statement of intent, or saying 'I do not forbid you,' does not make someone an agent. The author contrasts this with trade permission for a slave, where silence can imply authorization.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous expression
Read the scenario and locate the phrase used by the husband. Is it explicit like 'divorce her' or ambiguous like 'yes' or 'I do not forbid you'?
2
Classify the expression's legal effect
Determine whether the expression, by itself, amounts to delegation (tafwīḍ) according to Hanafi rules. Ambiguous expressions do not create agency unless intention (niyya) of delegation is proven.
The text gives specific examples: 'yes' after 'I want to divorce your wife' is not agency unless the husband intended delegation.
3
Compare with trade permission
Notice the contrast: telling a slave 'I do not forbid you from trade' is permission (idhn), but telling anyone 'I do not forbid you from divorcing my wife' is not agency. Understand the principle: trade is a common, ongoing activity where silence implies consent; divorce is a specific, one-time act requiring explicit authorization.
This is a qiyas ma‘a al-fariq (analogy with a difference) — the dissimilarity prevents the transfer of the ruling.
4
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Test your understanding: would seeing someone divorce your wife and not objecting create an agency? No, as stated in the text. The principle is consistent: passive behavior never creates agency for divorce.
5
Formulate the ruling
State the ruling: An ambiguous expression (like 'yes', 'I do not forbid you', silence) does not make the addressee an agent for divorce. Only explicit words of delegation (tafwīḍ) accompanied by intention have effect.
The relied-upon (muftā bihī) position is as in al-Khāniyya: no divorce occurs unless the husband intended delegation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيد بقوله «طلقها» لأنه لو قال له رجل أريد أن أطلق امرأتك ثلاثاً فقال الزوج نعم فقال الرجل طلقت امرأتك ثلاثاً، فالصحيح أن هذا كقول الرجل لامرأته نعم بعد قولها له أريد أن أطلق نفسي ثم طلقت نفسها من أ أنه لا يقع إلا إذا نوى الزوج التفويض إليها، وإن عنى بذلك طلقي نفسك إن استطعت أو طلقها إن استطعت لا تطلق كما في الخانية. ولو قال لا أنهاك عن طلاق امرأتي لا يكون توكيلاً، ولو قال لعبده لا أنهاك عن التجارة يكون إذناً في التجارة لأن قوله للعبد ذلك لا يكون دون ما لو رآه . ويشتري ولم ينهه وثمة يصير مأذوناً في التجارة فههنا أولى. ولو رأى انساناً يطلق امرأته ولم لا يصير المطلق وكيلاً ولا يقع كذلك هنا
And he restricted by his saying 'divorce her' because if a man said to him 'I want to divorce your wife three times' and the husband said 'yes', then the man said 'I have divorced your wife three times', the correct view is that this is like a man saying to his wife 'yes' after she said 'I want to divorce myself', then she divorced herself: it does not occur unless the husband intended delegation to her. And if he meant by that 'divorce yourself if you can' or 'divorce her if you can', she is not divorced as in al-Khaniyyah. And if he said 'I do not forbid you from divorcing my wife', it is not an agency. And if he said to his slave 'I do not forbid you from trade', it is permission for trade, because his saying that to the slave is not less than if he saw him buying and did not prohibit him, and there he becomes authorized in trade, so here it is more fitting. And if he saw a person divorcing his wife and did not [intervene], the divorcer does not become an agent and it does not occur, likewise here.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses ambiguous expressions in creating an agency for divorce. The first example: a man says 'I want to divorce your wife,' and the husband says 'yes' without explicit delegation. The correct ruling is that this does not create agency unless the husband intended to delegate. The analogy is with a wife who says 'I want to divorce myself' and the husband says 'yes' — that does not give her the right to divorce unless he intended to delegate. The text also compares saying 'I do not forbid you' to a wife versus a slave. For a slave, it implies permission to trade, but for divorce, it does not create agency because divorce is not a common matter. The principle is that mere silence or non-prohibition does not create agency for divorce, unlike trade for a slave. This guards against assuming agency from weak statements.

Key Terms
تفويض (tafwīḍ): Delegation; the husband's explicit delegation to the wife or another to effect divorce
إذن (idhn): Permission; here used for trade with a slave, which is broader than agency for divorce
وكيل (wakīl): Agent; one authorized to act on behalf of another, requiring clear expression

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The divorce is valid because permission was given
B) The divorce is invalid because this does not create agency
C) The divorce is valid only if the husband was present
D) The divorce is valid only if the wife consents

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, divorce agency is only created by explicit, unambiguous delegation, not by passive or permissive expressions.

Scope of General Agency and Its Effect on Divorce
Listing rulings on general agency's scope in divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a general agent can divorce the principal's wife and apply the custom-based interpretation of general agency.

Core Idea
A general agent cannot divorce the principal's wife unless the agency was made in the context of discussing divorce.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical question: when a principal says 'I appoint you in all my affairs,' does that include the authority to divorce his wife? The Hanafi school answers with a nuanced distinction based on custom (urf) and the context of the conversation. We will examine the disagreement among Hanafi authorities and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What happens when a principal gives a general agency and the agent divorces the wife? Note that the text says there is disagreement.
The core issue is whether general wording covers divorce.
2
Analyze the disagreement
Understand the different positions: Abu Hanifa restricts general agency to commutative contracts; Muhammad includes gifts and leases; the correct view is that it does not cover divorce unless in context.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Understand the role of custom
See how the principal's profession affects the scope: for a merchant, it's trade; for a person with no known profession, the agency may be void.
Custom restricts the literal generality.
4
Recognize the exception
If the agency is made in the context of discussing divorce, then the agent has authority to divorce.
Context overrides the general rule.
5
Derive the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that general agency does not include divorce unless in the context of divorce.
This is clearly stated as 'al-sahih' in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال وكلتك في جميع أموري فطلق الوكيل امرأته اختلفوا فيه والصحيح أنه لا يقع. وفي فتاوى الفقيه أبي جعفر: لو قال وكلتك في جميع أموري وأقمتك مقام نفسي لم تكن الوكالة عامة، وإن كان أمر الرجل مختلفاً ليس له صناعة معروفة فالوكالة باطلة وإن كان الموكل تاجراً ينصرف التوكيل إلى التجارة قال رحمه الله : ولو قال وكلتك في جميع أموري التي يجوز بها التوكيل كانت الوكالة عامة في جميع البياعات والأنكحة وكل شيء. وعن محمد : لو قال هو وكيلي في كل شيء جائز صنعه كان وكيلاً في البياعات والهبات والإجارات. وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يكون وكيلاً في المعاوضات دون الهبات والعتاق وقال :مولانا وهذا كله إذا لم يكن في حال مذاكرة الطلاق، فإن كان في حال مذاكرة الطلاق يكون وكيلاً بالطلاق. كذا في الخانية وأطلق في فعل الوكيل فشمل ما إذا سكر فطلق فإنه يقع على الصحيح كما في الخانية. وفيها من فصل التوكيل بالطلاق منه مسائل مهمة لا بأس بذكرها تكثيراً للفوائد منها : الوكيل بالطلاق والعتاق أو غيرهما إذا قبل التوكيل وغاب الموكل فإن الوكيل لا يجبر على فعل ما وكل فيه إلا فيما إذا قال له ادفع هذه العين إلى فلان فإنه يجبر على دفعه لأن الشيء المعين جاز أن يكون أمانة عند الآمر فيجب عليه تسليم الأمانة، وأما في غيره من الطلاق وغيره إنما أمره بالتصرف في ملك الآمر وليس على الأمر إيقاع الطلاق والعتاق فلا يجب على الوكيل ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأته بطلبها عند السفر وسافر ثم عزله بغير محضر المرأة، الصحيح أنه يملك عزله لأنه لا يجب عليه بطلبها . ومنها لو وكله بالطلاق ثم قال كلما عزلتك فأنت وكيلي قيل لا يصح التوكيل لأن فيه تغيير حكم الشرع والصحيح صحته، ثم قيل لا يملك عزله والصحيح أنه يملكه. وفي طريق عزله أقوال ؛ قال السرخسي : بقول عزلتك عن جميع الوكالات فينصرف إلى المعلق والمنجز، وقيل يقول عزلتك كلما وكلتك وقيل يقول رجعت عن الوكالات المعلقة وعزلتك عن الوكالات المطلقة ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأتيه فطلق إحداهما طلقت. ومنها لو وكله ليطلقها للسنة فطلقها في غير وقت السنة لا يقع لا للحال ولا إذا جاء وقت السنة لا يخرج عن الوكالة حتى لو طلقها بعد ذلك في وقت السنة يقع. ومنها لو طلقها الموكل ولو بائناً فطلاق الوكيل واقع ما دامت العدة ولا ينعزل بإبانة الموكل إذا لم يكن طلاق الوكيل بمال، فلو لم يطلقها الوكيل حتى تزوجها الموكل في العدة وقع طلاق الوكيل، وإن تزوجها بعد العدة لم يقع، وكذا لو طلقها الوكيل بعد ردة أحدهما ما دامت في العدة إلا إذا قضى بلحاقه فحينئذ تبطل الوكالة وارتداد الوكيل لا يبطلها إلا بالقضاء بلحاقه ومنها لو قال له إذا تزوجت فلانة فطلقها صح لصحة تعليق الوكالة. ومنها لو وكله بالطلاق فطلق قبل العلم لم يقع. ومنها لو وكله فرد ثم طلق لم يقع ولو سكت بلا قبول ثم طلق وقع ومنها لو شرط الخيار للموكل أو غيره في الوكالة صحت وبطل الشرط، ولا فرق بين وكالة ووكالة. ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأته وله أربع فطلق الوكيل واحدة بغير عينها، أو قال طلقت امرأتك فالبيان إلى الزوج، ولو طلق الوكيل معينة جاز ولا يقبل من الزوج أنه ما أرادها كما لو وكله ببيع عبد من عبيده فباع عبداً بعينه ومنها لو قال له طلقها غداً فقال الوكيل أنت طالق غداً كان باطلاً، ولو قال طلقها فقال الوكيل أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار فدخلت لم يقع، وإن قال طلقها ثلاثاً للسنة فقال الوكيل في طهر لم يجامعها فيه أنت طالق ثلاثاً للسنة . يقع للحال واحدة ويبطل الباقي، وقيل على قياس قول أبي حنيفة ينبغي أن لا يقع شيء لأنه مأمور بإيقاع الواحدة في كل طهر. وعنده المأمور بالواحدة إذا أوقع الثلاث لا يقع شيء والأصح أنه يقع هنا واحدة بلا خلاف لأن عند أبي حنيفة تعتبر الموافقة من حيث اللفظ فإن الرجل إذا قال لغيره طلق امرأتي ثلاثاً فطلقها ألفاً لا يصح، وكذا لو قال لغيره طلق امرأتي نصف تطليقة فطلقها الوكيل تطليقة لا يقع شيء، وهنا وجدت الموافقة من حيث اللفظ فيقع واحدة. ولو قال طلقها ثلاثاً للسنة بألف فقال لها الوكيل في وقت السنة أنت طالق ثلاثاً بألف فقبلت يقع واحدة بثلث الألف، فإن طلقها الوكيل في الطهر الثاني تطليقة بثلث الألف فقبلت يقع أخرى بغير شيء، وكذا لو طلقها الثالثة في الطهر الثالث ولو طلقها الوكيل أولاً تطليقة بثلث الألف ثم تزوجها الزوج ثم طلقها الوكيل تطليقة ثانية بثلث الألف تقع الثانية بثلث الألف، وكذا الثالثة على هذا الوجه ومنها لو وكله بطلاق المبانة بألف فطلقها الوكيل بألف
And if he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs' and the agent divorced his wife, there is disagreement and the correct view is that it does not occur. In the fatwas of al-Faqih Abu Ja'far: If he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs and I place you in my own position', the agency is not general; if the man's affairs are diverse and he has no known profession, the agency is void; if the principal is a merchant, the agency is restricted to trade. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: And if he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs in which agency is permissible', the agency is general in all sales, marriages, and everything. From Muhammad: If he said 'He is my agent in everything permissible for him to do', he is an agent in sales, gifts, and leases. From Abu Hanifa: He is an agent in commutative contracts but not gifts or manumissions. And our master said: All this is when not in the context of discussing divorce; if in the context of discussing divorce, he is an agent for divorce. Thus in al-Khaniyyah. And he (the author) spoke generally about the agent's action, including if he was intoxicated and divorced: it occurs according to the correct view as in al-Khaniyyah. In it from the section on agency for divorce are important issues; it is good to mention them to multiply benefits. Among them: The agent for divorce, manumission, or other things, if he accepted the agency and the principal is absent, the agent is not compelled to do what he is appointed for except if he said 'hand over this specific thing to so-and-so', then he is compelled because the specific thing may be a trust with the principal and he must deliver the trust. As for other than that, like divorce etc., he only ordered him to act in the principal's property, and the principal is not obliged to effect divorce or manumission, so the agent is not compelled. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce his wife upon her request during travel, and he traveled, then dismissed him without the wife's presence, the correct view is that he has the right to dismiss him because it is not obligatory upon him due to her request. Among them: If he appointed him for divorce, then said 'Whenever I dismiss you, you are my agent', it is said that the agency is not valid because it changes the rule of Shari'ah; the correct view is its validity. Then it is said he cannot dismiss him; the correct view is that he can. Regarding the method of dismissal, there are sayings: al-Sarakhsi said: By saying 'I dismiss you from all agencies', it applies to both conditional and unconditional. And it is said: He says 'I dismiss you whenever I appoint you'. And it is said: He says 'I retract from the conditional agencies and dismiss you from the unconditional agencies'. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce his two wives, and he divorced one, it occurs. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce her according to the Sunnah, and he divorced her at a time other than the time of the Sunnah, it does not occur immediately, nor when the time of the Sunnah comes; he does not exit the agency, so if he divorces her later at the time of the Sunnah, it occurs. Among them: If the principal divorced her, even with a irrevocable divorce, the agent's divorce is effective as long as the waiting period lasts, and he is not dismissed by the principal's irrevocable divorce if the agent's divorce was not for compensation. So if the agent did not divorce her until the principal married her during the waiting period, the agent's divorce occurs; if he married her after the waiting period, it does not occur. Likewise, if the agent divorced her after apostasy of one of them as long as she is in the waiting period, except if a judgment of his joining [the Muslims] is made, then the agency becomes void. The apostasy of the agent does not void it except by judgment of his joining. Among them: If he said to him 'If you marry so-and-so, divorce her', it is valid because suspended agency is valid. Among them: If he appointed him for divorce, and he divorced before knowledge, it does not occur. Among them: If he appointed him and he refused, then he divorced, it does not occur; but if he remained silent without acceptance, then divorced, it occurs. Among them: If he stipulated an option for the principal or another in the agency, the agency is valid and the condition is void; there is no difference between one agency and another. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce his wife, and he has four wives, and the agent divorced one without specification, or said 'I have divorced your wife', the clarification is up to the husband; if the agent divorced a specific woman, it is permissible, and the husband's claim that he did not intend her is not accepted, just as if he appointed him to sell a slave from his slaves and he sold a specific slave. Among them: If he said to him 'Divorce her tomorrow', and the agent said 'You are divorced tomorrow', it is void. And if he said 'Divorce her', and the agent said 'You are divorced if you enter the house', and she entered, it does not occur. And if he said 'Divorce her three times according to the Sunnah', and the agent said in a purity in which he did not have intercourse with her 'You are divorced three times according to the Sunnah', it occurs immediately as one and the rest are void. It is said that by analogy with Abu Hanifa's view, nothing should occur because he was ordered to effect one in each purity; according to him, if the one ordered to effect one effects three, nothing occurs. The correct view is that one occurs without dispute, because according to Abu Hanifa, compliance is considered in terms of wording: if a man says to another 'Divorce my wife three times' and he divorces her a thousand times, it is not valid; likewise, if he says 'Divorce my wife half a divorce' and the agent effects one divorce, nothing occurs. Here, compliance in wording is found, so one occurs. And if he said 'Divorce her three times according to the Sunnah for a thousand', and the agent said to her at the time of the Sunnah 'You are divorced three times for a thousand', and she accepted, one divorce occurs with one-third of the thousand. If the agent divorced her in the second purity once for one-third of the thousand and she accepted, another occurs for nothing. Likewise, if he divorced her the third in the third purity. If the agent first divorced her once for one-third of the thousand, then the husband married her, then the agent divorced her a second time for one-third of the thousand, the second occurs with one-third of the thousand; likewise the third in this way. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce a woman who is made irrevocable [by the husband?] for a thousand, and the agent divorced her for a thousand.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a comprehensive list of rulings on agency in divorce (tawkīl bi al-ṭalāq). It begins with the pivotal issue of general agency: if a man says 'I appoint you in all my affairs' and the agent divorces his wife, there is disagreement. The correct view is that it does not occur unless in the context of discussing divorce. This is because general agency is understood by custom ('urf): for a merchant, it means trade; for others, it may be void. Abu Hanifa limits it to commutative contracts, while Muhammad includes gifts and leases. The passage then lists many specific scenarios: the agent is not compelled to act except for delivering a specific item; the husband can dismiss the agent even without the wife's presence; a conditional dismissal clause ('whenever I dismiss you, you are my agent') is valid but the husband can still dismiss; methods of dismissal; divorcing one of two wives; divorcing at the wrong time for sunnah divorce; effect of the principal's own divorce on the agent's authority; apostasy of either party; suspended agency; divorce before knowledge; refusal vs. silence; stipulating an option; specifying which wife; delaying to 'tomorrow'; conditional divorce by agent; exceeding the number of divorces ordered; and a complex case involving monetary consideration. Each ruling is carefully conditioned. The passage is rich for memorization and application.

Key Terms
وكالة عامة (wakālah 'āmmah): General agency in all affairs; its scope is determined by custom, not literal wording
مذاكرة الطلاق (mudhakarat al-ṭalāq): Context of discussing divorce; if agency is given in this context, it includes divorce
عرف ('urf): Custom; used to interpret the scope of general agency

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if a man says to his agent 'I appoint you in all my affairs' and the agent divorces the wife without any prior discussion of divorce, what is the ruling?
A) The divorce occurs because the agency was general.
B) The divorce does not occur.
C) The divorce occurs only if the wife was present.
D) The divorce occurs only if the husband also divorces.

Key Takeaway
General agency in the Hanafi school is interpreted by custom, and divorce is not covered unless the agency is given in the context of discussing divorce.

Dismissal ('Azl) of the Agent: Conditions and Methods
Listing rulings on dismissal of agent in divorce agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the validity of an agent's dismissal and apply the different methods of dismissal as per the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The principal can dismiss the agent at any time, even without the wife's presence, and a conditional dismissal clause does not prevent dismissal.

This passage discusses the principal's right to dismiss the agent ('azl) in a divorce agency. It covers scenarios such as dismissal during travel, conditional clauses, and the precise wording for effective dismissal. Understanding these rules ensures that the agency remains under the principal's control.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule of dismissal
The principal can dismiss the agent without needing the wife's presence. The text gives an example of dismissal during travel for a request-based agency.
Dismissal is a unilateral right.
2
Analyze the conditional dismissal clause
If the principal says 'Whenever I dismiss you, you are my agent,' the agency is valid but the principal can still dismiss. There is a saying that he cannot dismiss, but the correct view is that he can.
Such a clause does not take away the right of dismissal.
3
Learn the methods of dismissal
Three methods: (1) saying 'I dismiss you from all agencies' covers all, (2) 'I dismiss you whenever I appoint you', (3) 'I retract from conditional agencies and dismiss from unconditional ones'.
Different wordings affect which agencies are revoked.

ولو قال وكلتك في جميع أموري فطلق الوكيل امرأته اختلفوا فيه والصحيح أنه لا يقع. وفي فتاوى الفقيه أبي جعفر: لو قال وكلتك في جميع أموري وأقمتك مقام نفسي لم تكن الوكالة عامة، وإن كان أمر الرجل مختلفاً ليس الطلاق، فإن كان في حال مذاكرة الطلاق يكون وكيلاً بالطلاق. كذا في الخانية وأطلق في فعل الوكيل فشمل ما إذا سكر فطلق فإنه يقع على الصحيح كما في الخانية. وفيها من فصل التوكيل بالطلاق منه مسائل مهمة لا بأس الشيء المعين جاز أن يكون أمانة عند الآمر فيجب عليه تسليم الأمانة، وأما في غيره من الطلاق وغيره إنما أمره بالتصرف في ملك الآمر وليس على الأمر إيقاع الطلاق والعتاق فلا يجب على الوكيل ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأته بطلبها عند السفر وسافر ثم عزله بغير محضر المرأة، الصحيح أنه يملك عزله لأنه لا يجب عليه بطلبها . ومنها لو وكله بالطلاق ثم قال كلما عزلتك فأنت وكيلي قيل لا يصح التوكيل لأن فيه تغيير حكم الشرع والصحيح صحته، ثم قيل لا يملك عزله والصحيح أنه يملكه. وفي طريق عزله أقوال ؛ قال السرخسي : بقول عزلتك عن جميع الوكالات فينصرف إلى المعلق والمنجز، وقيل يقول عزلتك كلما وكلتك وقيل يقول رجعت عن الوكالات المعلقة وعزلتك عن الوكالات المطلقة ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأتيه فطلق إحداهما طلقت. ومنها لو وكله ليطلقها للسنة فطلقها في غير وقت السنة لا يقع لا للحال ولا إذا جاء وقت السنة لا يخرج عن الوكالة حتى لو طلقها بعد ذلك في وقت السنة يقع. ومنها لو طلقها الموكل ولو بائناً فطلاق الوكيل واقع ما دامت العدة ولا ينعزل بإبانة الموكل إذا لم يكن طلاق الوكيل بمال، فلو لم يطلقها الوكيل حتى تزوجها الموكل في العدة وقع طلاق الوكيل، وإن تزوجها بعد العدة لم يقع، وكذا لو طلقها الوكيل بعد ردة أحدهما ما دامت في العدة إلا إذا قضى بلحاقه فحينئذ تبطل الوكالة وارتداد الوكيل لا يبطلها إلا بالقضاء بلحاقه ومنها لو قال له إذا تزوجت فلانة فطلقها صح لصحة تعليق الوكالة. ومنها لو وكله بالطلاق فطلق قبل العلم لم يقع. ومنها لو وكله فرد ثم طلق لم يقع ولو سكت بلا قبول ثم طلق وقع ومنها لو شرط الخيار للموكل أو غيره في الوكالة صحت وبطل الشرط، ولا فرق بين وكالة ووكالة. ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأته وله أربع فطلق الوكيل واحدة بغير عينها، أو قال طلقت امرأتك فالبيان إلى الزوج، ولو طلق الوكيل معينة جاز ولا يقبل من الزوج أنه ما أرادها كما لو وكله ببيع عبد من عبيده فباع عبداً بعينه ومنها لو قال له طلقها غداً فقال الوكيل أنت طالق غداً كان باطلاً، ولو قال طلقها فقال الوكيل أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار فدخلت لم يقع، وإن قال طلقها ثلاثاً للسنة فقال الوكيل في طهر لم يجامعها فيه أنت طالق ثلاثاً للسنة . يقع للحال واحدة ويبطل الباقي، وقيل على قياس قول أبي حنيفة ينبغي أن لا يقع شيء لأنه مأمور بإيقاع الواحدة في كل طهر. وعنده المأمور بالواحدة إذا أوقع الثلاث لا يقع شيء والأصح أنه يقع هنا واحدة بلا خلاف لأن عند أبي حنيفة تعتبر الموافقة من حيث اللفظ فإن الرجل إذا قال لغيره طلق امرأتي ثلاثاً فطلقها ألفاً لا يصح، وكذا لو قال لغيره طلق امرأتي نصف تطليقة فطلقها الوكيل تطليقة لا يقع شيء، وهنا وجدت الموافقة من حيث اللفظ فيقع واحدة. ولو قال طلقها ثلاثاً للسنة بألف فقال لها الوكيل في وقت السنة أنت طالق ثلاثاً بألف فقبلت يقع واحدة بثلث الألف، فإن طلقها الوكيل في الطهر الثاني تطليقة بثلث الألف فقبلت يقع أخرى بغير شيء، وكذا لو طلقها الثالثة في الطهر الثالث ولو طلقها الوكيل أولاً تطليقة بثلث الألف ثم تزوجها الزوج ثم طلقها الوكيل تطليقة ثانية بثلث الألف تقع الثانية بثلث الألف، وكذا الثالثة على هذا الوجه ومنها لو وكله بطلاق المبانة بألف فطلقها الوكيل بألف
And if he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs' and the agent divorced his wife, there is disagreement and the correct view is that it does not occur. In the fatwas of al-Faqih Abu Ja'far: If he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs and I place you in my own position', the agency is not general; if the man's affairs are diverse and he has no known profession, the agency is void; if the principal is a merchant, the agency is restricted to trade. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: And if he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs in which agency is permissible', the agency is general in all sales, marriages, and everything. From Muhammad: If he said 'He is my agent in everything permissible for him to do', he is an agent in sales, gifts, and leases. From Abu Hanifa: He is an agent in commutative contracts but not gifts or manumissions. A) The agency is invalid because it changes the Shari'ah.
