Divorce by Agent: Timing, Principal's Actions, and Apostasy
Listing rulings on timing, principal's divorce, and apostasy affecting agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the validity of a divorce by an agent when it occurs at an improper time, after the principal's own divorce, or after apostasy.

Core Idea
An agent's divorce is ineffective if done outside the sunnah time, but the agency remains; a principal's own divorce does not terminate the agency unless it is a divorce for compensation.

This passage covers several scenarios that affect the validity of an agent's divorce: timing relative to the sunnah, the principal's own divorce, and apostasy of either party. These rulings ensure that the agent's authority is clearly delineated and that the divorce is effective only under proper conditions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the effect of improper timing
If the agent divorces at a time other than the sunnah time (e.g., during menstruation), the divorce does not occur immediately, but the agent is not dismissed; he can still divorce later at the correct time.
Agency continues even if the agent errs in timing.
2
Analyze the effect of principal's own divorce
If the principal divorces his wife (even with a irrevocable divorce), the agent's authority remains during the waiting period. The agent's divorce is effective unless the principal's divorce was for compensation (in which case the agent might be dismissed).
The agency is not automatically terminated by the principal's action.
3
Examine the effect of apostasy
If either party apostatizes during the waiting period, the agent's divorce is effective except if a judgment of joining the Muslims is made (which voids the agency). Apostasy of the agent alone does not void the agency until a judgment.
Apostasy does not automatically invalidate the agency; a judicial decision is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال وكلتك في جميع أموري فطلق الوكيل امرأته اختلفوا فيه والصحيح أنه لا يقع. وفي فتاوى الفقيه أبي جعفر: لو قال وكلتك في جميع أموري وأقمتك مقام نفسي لم تكن الوكالة عامة، وإن كان أمر الرجل مختلفاً ليس له صناعة معروفة فالوكالة باطلة وإن كان الموكل تاجراً ينصرف التوكيل إلى التجارة قال رحمه الله : ولو قال وكلتك في جميع أموري التي يجوز بها التوكيل كانت الوكالة عامة في جميع البياعات والأنكحة وكل شيء. وعن محمد : لو قال هو وكيلي في كل شيء جائز صنعه كان وكيلاً في البياعات والهبات والإجارات. وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يكون وكيلاً في المعاوضات دون الهبات والعتاق وقال :مولانا وهذا كله إذا لم يكن في حال مذاكرة الطلاق، فإن كان في حال مذاكرة الطلاق يكون وكيلاً بالطلاق. كذا في الخانية وأطلق في فعل الوكيل فشمل ما إذا سكر فطلق فإنه يقع على الصحيح كما في الخانية. وفيها من فصل التوكيل بالطلاق منه مسائل مهمة لا بأس بذكرها تكثيراً للفوائد منها : الوكيل بالطلاق والعتاق أو غيرهما إذا قبل التوكيل وغاب الموكل فإن الوكيل لا يجبر على فعل ما وكل فيه إلا فيما إذا قال له ادفع هذه العين إلى فلان فإنه يجبر على دفعه لأن الشيء المعين جاز أن يكون أمانة عند الآمر فيجب عليه تسليم الأمانة، وأما في غيره من الطلاق وغيره إنما أمره بالتصرف في ملك الآمر وليس على الأمر إيقاع الطلاق والعتاق فلا يجب على الوكيل ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأته بطلبها عند السفر وسافر ثم عزله بغير محضر المرأة، الصحيح أنه يملك عزله لأنه لا يجب عليه بطلبها . ومنها لو وكله بالطلاق ثم قال كلما عزلتك فأنت وكيلي قيل لا يصح التوكيل لأن فيه تغيير حكم الشرع والصحيح صحته، ثم قيل لا يملك عزله والصحيح أنه يملكه. وفي طريق عزله أقوال ؛ قال السرخسي : بقول عزلتك عن جميع الوكالات فينصرف إلى المعلق والمنجز، وقيل يقول عزلتك كلما وكلتك وقيل يقول رجعت عن الوكالات المعلقة وعزلتك عن الوكالات المطلقة ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأتيه فطلق إحداهما طلقت. ومنها لو وكله ليطلقها للسنة فطلقها في غير وقت السنة لا يقع لا للحال ولا إذا جاء وقت السنة لا يخرج عن الوكالة حتى لو طلقها بعد ذلك في وقت السنة يقع. ومنها لو طلقها الموكل ولو بائناً فطلاق الوكيل واقع ما دامت العدة ولا ينعزل بإبانة الموكل إذا لم يكن طلاق الوكيل بمال، فلو لم يطلقها الوكيل حتى تزوجها الموكل في العدة وقع طلاق الوكيل، وإن تزوجها بعد العدة لم يقع، وكذا لو طلقها الوكيل بعد ردة أحدهما ما دامت في العدة إلا إذا قضى بلحاقه فحينئذ تبطل الوكالة وارتداد الوكيل لا يبطلها إلا بالقضاء بلحاقه ومنها لو قال له إذا تزوجت فلانة فطلقها صح لصحة تعليق الوكالة. ومنها لو وكله بالطلاق فطلق قبل العلم لم يقع. ومنها لو وكله فرد ثم طلق لم يقع ولو سكت بلا قبول ثم طلق وقع ومنها لو شرط الخيار للموكل أو غيره في الوكالة صحت وبطل الشرط، ولا فرق بين وكالة ووكالة. ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأته وله أربع فطلق الوكيل واحدة بغير عينها، أو قال طلقت امرأتك فالبيان إلى الزوج، ولو طلق الوكيل معينة جاز ولا يقبل من الزوج أنه ما أرادها كما لو وكله ببيع عبد من عبيده فباع عبداً بعينه ومنها لو قال له طلقها غداً فقال الوكيل أنت طالق غداً كان باطلاً، ولو قال طلقها فقال الوكيل أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار فدخلت لم يقع، وإن قال طلقها ثلاثاً للسنة فقال الوكيل في طهر لم يجامعها فيه أنت طالق ثلاثاً للسنة . يقع للحال واحدة ويبطل الباقي، وقيل على قياس قول أبي حنيفة ينبغي أن لا يقع شيء لأنه مأمور بإيقاع الواحدة في كل طهر. وعنده المأمور بالواحدة إذا أوقع الثلاث لا يقع شيء والأصح أنه يقع هنا واحدة بلا خلاف لأن عند أبي حنيفة تعتبر الموافقة من حيث اللفظ فإن الرجل إذا قال لغيره طلق امرأتي ثلاثاً فطلقها ألفاً لا يصح، وكذا لو قال لغيره طلق امرأتي نصف تطليقة فطلقها الوكيل تطليقة لا يقع شيء، وهنا وجدت الموافقة من حيث اللفظ فيقع واحدة. ولو قال طلقها ثلاثاً للسنة بألف فقال لها الوكيل في وقت السنة أنت طالق ثلاثاً بألف فقبلت يقع واحدة بثلث الألف، فإن طلقها الوكيل في الطهر الثاني تطليقة بثلث الألف فقبلت يقع أخرى بغير شيء، وكذا لو طلقها الثالثة في الطهر الثالث ولو طلقها الوكيل أولاً تطليقة بثلث الألف ثم تزوجها الزوج ثم طلقها الوكيل تطليقة ثانية بثلث الألف تقع الثانية بثلث الألف، وكذا الثالثة على هذا الوجه ومنها لو وكله بطلاق المبانة بألف فطلقها الوكيل بألف
And if he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs' and the agent divorced his wife, there is disagreement and the correct view is that it does not occur. In the fatwas of al-Faqih Abu Ja'far: If he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs and I place you in my own position', the agency is not general; if the man's affairs are diverse and he has no known profession, the agency is void; if the principal is a merchant, the agency is restricted to trade. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: And if he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs in which agency is permissible', the agency is general in all sales, marriages, and everything. From Muhammad: If he said 'He is my agent in everything permissible for him to do', he is an agent in sales, gifts, and leases. From Abu Hanifa: He is an agent in commutative contracts but not gifts or manumissions. And our master said: All this is when not in the context of discussing divorce; if in the context of discussing divorce, he is an agent for divorce. Thus in al-Khaniyyah. And he (the author) spoke generally about the agent's action, including if he was intoxicated and divorced: it occurs according to the correct view as in al-Khaniyyah. In it from the section on agency for divorce are important issues; it is good to mention them to multiply benefits. Among them: The agent for divorce, manumission, or other things, if he accepted the agency and the principal is absent, the agent is not compelled to do what he is appointed for except if he said 'hand over this specific thing to so-and-so', then he is compelled because the specific thing may be a trust with the principal and he must deliver the trust. As for other than that, like divorce etc., he only ordered him to act in the principal's property, and the principal is not obliged to effect divorce or manumission, so the agent is not compelled. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce his wife upon her request during travel, and he traveled, then dismissed him without the wife's presence, the correct view is that he has the right to dismiss him because it is not obligatory upon him due to her request. Among them: If he appointed him for divorce, then said 'Whenever I dismiss you, you are my agent', it is said that the agency is not valid because it changes the rule of Shari'ah; the correct view is its validity. Then it is said he cannot dismiss him; the correct view is that he can. Regarding the method of dismissal, there are sayings: al-Sarakhsi said: By saying 'I dismiss you from all agencies', it applies to both conditional and unconditional. And it is said: He says 'I dismiss you whenever I appoint you'. And it is said: He says 'I retract from the conditional agencies and dismiss you from the unconditional agencies'. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce his two wives, and he divorced one, it occurs. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce her according to the Sunnah, and he divorced her at a time other than the time of the Sunnah, it does not occur immediately, nor when the time of the Sunnah comes; he does not exit the agency, so if he divorces her later at the time of the Sunnah, it occurs. Among them: If the principal divorced her, even with a irrevocable divorce, the agent's divorce is effective as long as the waiting period lasts, and he is not dismissed by the principal's irrevocable divorce if the agent's divorce was not for compensation. So if the agent did not divorce her until the principal married her during the waiting period, the agent's divorce occurs; if he married her after the waiting period, it does not occur. Likewise, if the agent divorced her after apostasy of one of them as long as she is in the waiting period, except if a judgment of his joining [the Muslims] is made, then the agency becomes void. The apostasy of the agent does not void it except by judgment of his joining. Among them: If he said to him 'If you marry so-and-so, divorce her', it is valid because suspended agency is valid. Among them: If he appointed him for divorce, and he divorced before knowledge, it does not occur. Among them: If he appointed him and he refused, then he divorced, it does not occur; but if he remained silent without acceptance, then divorced, it occurs. Among them: If he stipulated an option for the principal or another in the agency, the agency is valid and the condition is void; there is no difference between one agency and another. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce his wife, and he has four wives, and the agent divorced one without specification, or said 'I have divorced your wife', the clarification is up to the husband; if the agent divorced a specific woman, it is permissible, and the husband's claim that he did not intend her is not accepted, just as if he appointed him to sell a slave from his slaves and he sold a specific slave. Among them: If he said to him 'Divorce her tomorrow', and the agent said 'You are divorced tomorrow', it is void. And if he said 'Divorce her', and the agent said 'You are divorced if you enter the house', and she entered, it does not occur. And if he said 'Divorce her three times according to the Sunnah', and the agent said in a purity in which he did not have intercourse with her 'You are divorced three times according to the Sunnah', it occurs immediately as one and the rest are void. It is said that by analogy with Abu Hanifa's view, nothing should occur because he was ordered to effect one in each purity; according to him, if the one ordered to effect one effects three, nothing occurs. The correct view is that one occurs without dispute, because according to Abu Hanifa, compliance is considered in terms of wording: if a man says to another 'Divorce my wife three times' and he divorces her a thousand times, it is not valid; likewise, if he says 'Divorce my wife half a divorce' and the agent effects one divorce, nothing occurs. Here, compliance in wording is found, so one occurs. And if he said 'Divorce her three times according to the Sunnah for a thousand', and the agent said to her at the time of the Sunnah 'You are divorced three times for a thousand', and she accepted, one divorce occurs with one-third of the thousand. If the agent divorced her in the second purity once for one-third of the thousand and she accepted, another occurs for nothing. Likewise, if he divorced her the third in the third purity. If the agent first divorced her once for one-third of the thousand, then the husband married her, then the agent divorced her a second time for one-third of the thousand, the second occurs with one-third of the thousand; likewise the third in this way. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce a woman who is made irrevocable [by the husband?] for a thousand, and the agent divorced her for a thousand.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a comprehensive list of rulings on agency in divorce (tawkīl bi al-ṭalāq). It begins with the pivotal issue of general agency: if a man says 'I appoint you in all my affairs' and the agent divorces his wife, there is disagreement. The correct view is that it does not occur unless in the context of discussing divorce. This is because general agency is understood by custom ('urf): for a merchant, it means trade; for others, it may be void. Abu Hanifa limits it to commutative contracts, while Muhammad includes gifts and leases. The passage then lists many specific scenarios: the agent is not compelled to act except for delivering a specific item; the husband can dismiss the agent even without the wife's presence; a conditional dismissal clause ('whenever I dismiss you, you are my agent') is valid but the husband can still dismiss; methods of dismissal; divorcing one of two wives; divorcing at the wrong time for sunnah divorce; effect of the principal's own divorce on the agent's authority; apostasy of either party; suspended agency; divorce before knowledge; refusal vs. silence; stipulating an option; specifying which wife; delaying to 'tomorrow'; conditional divorce by agent; exceeding the number of divorces ordered; and a complex case involving monetary consideration. Each ruling is carefully conditioned. The passage is rich for memorization and application.

Key Terms
سنة الطلاق (sunnat al-ṭalāq): The Sunnah method of divorce: one pronouncement in a purity without intercourse
عدة ('iddah): Waiting period after divorce
ردة (riddah): Apostasy from Islam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if an agent appointed to divorce according to the Sunnah divorces the wife during her menstruation, what is the effect?
A) The divorce is valid and effective immediately.
B) The divorce is invalid and the agency is terminated.
C) The divorce is invalid for now, but the agent remains authorized and can divorce later at the correct time.
D) The divorce is valid only if the wife accepts.

Key Takeaway
An agent's divorce at a non-sunnah time is ineffective but the agency continues; the principal's own divorce does not dismiss the agent during the iddah.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Refusal, Silence, Option, Specifying Wives, and Conditional Divorce
Listing rulings on refusal, silence, option, and specification in divorce agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the validity of an agent's divorce after refusal, silence, stipulation of an option, and in cases of unspecified wives or conditional pronouncements.

Core Idea
An agent's divorce is invalid after refusal, but valid after silence; a stipulation of an option in the agency is void; the agent's divorce of a specific wife is effective even if the husband claims otherwise.

This passage addresses more detailed scenarios in divorce agency: the agent's response (refusal vs. silence), the effect of stipulating an option for the principal, how to handle multiple wives, and the effect of the agent adding a condition to the divorce. These rulings ensure clarity in the agent's authority and the finality of the divorce.

Guided Path
1
Differentiate between refusal and silence
If the agent refuses the agency and later divorces, the divorce does not occur. If he remains silent without acceptance and then divorces, it does occur.
Silence is considered tacit acceptance in agency.
2
Analyze the stipulation of an option
If the principal stipulates an option for himself or another in the agency, the agency is valid but the condition is void.
Agency is a binding contract; options do not apply.
3
Handle unspecified wives
If the husband has multiple wives and the agent divorces one without specifying, or says 'I have divorced your wife', the clarification is up to the husband. If the agent specifies a particular wife, it is effective and the husband's claim that he did not intend her is not accepted.
The agent's specification is binding.
4
Examine conditional divorce by agent
If the principal says 'Divorce her' and the agent says 'You are divorced if you enter the house', and she enters, the divorce does not occur because the agent exceeded his authority.
The agent cannot add conditions to the divorce.

ولو قال وكلتك في جميع أموري فطلق الوكيل امرأته اختلفوا فيه والصحيح أنه لا يقع. وفي فتاوى الفقيه أبي جعفر: لو قال وكلتك في جميع أموري وأقمتك مقام نفسي لم تكن الوكالة عامة، وإن كان أمر الرجل مختلفاً ليس له صناعة معروفة فالوكالة باطلة وإن كان الموكل تاجراً ينصرف التوكيل إلى التجارة قال رحمه الله : ولو قال وكلتك في جميع أموري التي يجوز بها التوكيل كانت الوكالة عامة في جميع البياعات والأنكحة وكل شيء. المعلقة وعزلتك عن الوكالات المطلقة ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأتيه فطلق إحداهما طلقت. ومنها لو وكله ليطلقها للسنة فطلقها في غير وقت السنة لا يقع لا للحال ولا إذا جاء وقت السنة لا يخرج عن الوكالة حتى لو كما لو وكله ببيع عبد من عبيده فباع عبداً بعينه ومنها لو قال له طلقها غداً فقال الوكيل أنت طالق غداً كان باطلاً، ولو قال طلقها فقال الوكيل أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار فدخلت لم يقع، وإن قال طلقها ثلاثاً للسنة فقال الوكيل في طهر لم يجامعها فيه أنت طالق ثلاثاً للسنة . يقع للحال واحدة ويبطل الباقي، وقيل على قياس قول أبي حنيفة ينبغي أن لا يقع شيء لأنه مأمور بإيقاع الواحدة في كل طهر. وعنده المأمور بالواحدة إذا أوقع الثلاث لا يقع شيء والأصح أنه يقع هنا واحدة بلا خلاف لأن عند أبي حنيفة تعتبر الموافقة من حيث اللفظ فإن الرجل إذا قال لغيره طلق امرأتي ثلاثاً فطلقها ألفاً لا يصح، وكذا لو قال لغيره طلق امرأتي نصف تطليقة فطلقها الوكيل تطليقة لا يقع شيء، وهنا وجدت الموافقة من حيث اللفظ فيقع واحدة. ولو قال طلقها ثلاثاً للسنة بألف فقال لها الوكيل في وقت السنة أنت طالق ثلاثاً بألف فقبلت يقع واحدة بثلث الألف، فإن طلقها الوكيل في الطهر الثاني تطليقة بثلث الألف فقبلت يقع أخرى بغير شيء، وكذا لو طلقها الثالثة في الطهر الثالث ولو طلقها الوكيل أولاً تطليقة بثلث الألف ثم تزوجها الزوج ثم طلقها الوكيل تطليقة ثانية بثلث الألف تقع الثانية بثلث الألف، وكذا الثالثة على هذا الوجه ومنها لو وكله بطلاق المبانة بألف فطلقها الوكيل بألف
And if he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs' and the agent divorced his wife, there is disagreement and the correct view is that it does not occur. In the fatwas of al-Faqih Abu Ja'far: If he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs and I place you in my own position', the agency is not general; if the man's affairs are diverse and he has no known profession, the agency is void; if the principal is a merchant, the agency is restricted to trade. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: And if he said 'I appoint you as agent in all my affairs in which agency is permissible', the agency is general in all sales, marriages, and everything. From Muhammad: If he said 'He is my agent in everything permissible for him to do', he is an agent in sales, gifts, and leases. From Abu Hanifa: He is an agent in commutative contracts but not gifts or manumissions. And our master said: All this is when not in the context of discussing divorce; if in the context of discussing divorce, he is an agent for divorce. Thus in al-Khaniyyah. And he (the author) spoke generally about the agent's action, including if he was intoxicated and divorced: it occurs according to the correct view as in al-Khaniyyah. In it from the section on agency for divorce are important issues; it is good to mention them to multiply benefits. Among them: The agent for divorce, manumission, or other things, if he accepted the agency and the principal is absent, the agent is not compelled to do what he is appointed for except if he said 'hand over this specific thing to so-and-so', then he is compelled because the specific thing may be a trust with the principal and he must deliver the trust. As for other than that, like divorce etc., he only ordered him to act in the principal's property, and the principal is not obliged to effect divorce or manumission, so the agent is not compelled. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce his wife upon her request during travel, and he traveled, then dismissed him without the wife's presence, the correct view is that he has the right to dismiss him because it is not obligatory upon him due to her request. Among them: If he appointed him for divorce, then said 'Whenever I dismiss you, you are my agent', it is said that the agency is not valid because it changes the rule of Shari'ah; the correct view is its validity. Then it is said he cannot dismiss him; the correct view is that he can. Regarding the method of dismissal, there are sayings: al-Sarakhsi said: By saying 'I dismiss you from all agencies', it applies to both conditional and unconditional. And it is said: He says 'I dismiss you whenever I appoint you'. And it is said: He says 'I retract from the conditional agencies and dismiss you from the unconditional agencies'. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce his two wives, and he divorced one, it occurs. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce her according to the Sunnah, and he divorced her at a time other than the time of the Sunnah, it does not occur immediately, nor when the time of the Sunnah comes; he does not exit the agency, so if he divorces her later at the time of the Sunnah, it occurs. Among them: If the principal divorced her, even with a irrevocable divorce, the agent's divorce is effective as long as the waiting period lasts, and he is not dismissed by the principal's irrevocable divorce if the agent's divorce was not for compensation. So if the agent did not divorce her until the principal married her during the waiting period, the agent's divorce occurs; if he married her after the waiting period, it does not occur. Likewise, if the agent divorced her after apostasy of one of them as long as she is in the waiting period, except if a judgment of his joining [the Muslims] is made, then the agency becomes void. The apostasy of the agent does not void it except by judgment of his joining. Among them: If he said to him 'If you marry so-and-so, divorce her', it is valid because suspended agency is valid. Among them: If he appointed him for divorce, and he divorced before knowledge, it does not occur. Among them: If he appointed him and he refused, then he divorced, it does not occur; but if he remained silent without acceptance, then divorced, it occurs. Among them: If he stipulated an option for the principal or another in the agency, the agency is valid and the condition is void; there is no difference between one agency and another. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce his wife, and he has four wives, and the agent divorced one without specification, or said 'I have divorced your wife', the clarification is up to the husband; if the agent divorced a specific woman, it is permissible, and the husband's claim that he did not intend her is not accepted, just as if he appointed him to sell a slave from his slaves and he sold a specific slave. Among them: If he said to him 'Divorce her tomorrow', and the agent said 'You are divorced tomorrow', it is void. And if he said 'Divorce her', and the agent said 'You are divorced if you enter the house', and she entered, it does not occur. And if he said 'Divorce her three times according to the Sunnah', and the agent said in a purity in which he did not have intercourse with her 'You are divorced three times according to the Sunnah', it occurs immediately as one and the rest are void. It is said that by analogy with Abu Hanifa's view, nothing should occur because he was ordered to effect one in each purity; according to him, if the one ordered to effect one effects three, nothing occurs. The correct view is that one occurs without dispute, because according to Abu Hanifa, compliance is considered in terms of wording: if a man says to another 'Divorce my wife three times' and he divorces her a thousand times, it is not valid; likewise, if he says 'Divorce my wife half a divorce' and the agent effects one divorce, nothing occurs. Here, compliance in wording is found, so one occurs. And if he said 'Divorce her three times according to the Sunnah for a thousand', and the agent said to her at the time of the Sunnah 'You are divorced three times for a thousand', and she accepted, one divorce occurs with one-third of the thousand. If the agent divorced her in the second purity once for one-third of the thousand and she accepted, another occurs for nothing. Likewise, if he divorced her the third in the third purity. If the agent first divorced her once for one-third of the thousand, then the husband married her, then the agent divorced her a second time for one-third of the thousand, the second occurs with one-third of the thousand; likewise the third in this way. Among them: If he appointed him to divorce a woman who is made irrevocable [by the husband?] for a thousand, and the agent divorced her for a thousand.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a comprehensive list of rulings on agency in divorce (tawkīl bi al-ṭalāq). It begins with the pivotal issue of general agency: if a man says 'I appoint you in all my affairs' and the agent divorces his wife, there is disagreement. The correct view is that it does not occur unless in the context of discussing divorce. This is because general agency is understood by custom ('urf): for a merchant, it means trade; for others, it may be void. Abu Hanifa limits it to commutative contracts, while Muhammad includes gifts and leases. The passage then lists many specific scenarios: the agent is not compelled to act except for delivering a specific item; the husband can dismiss the agent even without the wife's presence; a conditional dismissal clause ('whenever I dismiss you, you are my agent') is valid but the husband can still dismiss; methods of dismissal; divorcing one of two wives; divorcing at the wrong time for sunnah divorce; effect of the principal's own divorce on the agent's authority; apostasy of either party; suspended agency; divorce before knowledge; refusal vs. silence; stipulating an option; specifying which wife; delaying to 'tomorrow'; conditional divorce by agent; exceeding the number of divorces ordered; and a complex case involving monetary consideration. Each ruling is carefully conditioned. The passage is rich for memorization and application.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyār): Option; a stipulation that gives a right to cancel
سكوت (sukūt): Silence; considered acceptance in agency

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if a husband appoints an agent to divorce his wife and stipulates an option for himself, what is the effect?
A) The agency is void.
B) The agency is valid, but the condition is void.
C) The agency is valid only if the wife agrees.
D) The agency is suspended until the option is exercised.

Key Takeaway
Silence after appointment is acceptance; an option condition in agency is void; the agent's specification of a wife is binding; and the agent cannot add conditions or delays to the divorce.

Talaq — Divorce

Agency in Divorce: Validity and Revocation
Commentary on agency in divorce focusing on revocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the validity of agency in divorce and explain the rulings on revocation, including the effect of a conditional revocation clause.

Core Idea
Agency in divorce combines wakalah and ta'liq; revocation is generally allowed but may become binding if tied to an oath.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores the intersection of agency and divorce. The author presents a series of rulings that clarify when an agent's divorce takes effect and how the principal can revoke the agency. Understanding these rules is crucial for ensuring that divorces are validly executed and that the principal retains control over the process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that agency in divorce is valid (sahih) and has elements of conditional divorce (ta'liq).
2
Analyze the revocation rules
The principal may revoke the agent even without the wife's presence; revocation is generally effective except in certain cases.
3
Examine the conditional revocation clause
If the principal says 'Whenever I revoke you, you are my agent,' the agency becomes binding and revocation is ineffective.
This is analogous to an oath.
4
Apply the methods of revocation
Al-Sarakhsi and others give specific wordings for revocation that cover both conditional and unconditional agencies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق فصل في المشيئة
السفر وسافر ثم عزله بغير محضر المرأة، الصحيح أنه يملك عزله لأنه لا يجب عليه بطلبها . ومنها لو وكله بالطلاق ثم قال كلما عزلتك فأنت وكيلي قيل لا يصح التوكيل لأن فيه تغيير حكم الشرع والصحيح صحته، ثم قيل لا يملك عزله والصحيح أنه يملكه. وفي طريق عزله أقوال ؛ قال السرخسي : بقول عزلتك عن جميع الوكالات فينصرف إلى المعلق والمنجز، وقيل يقول عزلتك كلما وكلتك وقيل يقول رجعت عن الوكالات المعلقة وعزلتك عن الوكالات المطلقة ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأتيه فطلق إحداهما طلقت. ومنها لو وكله ليطلقها للسنة فطلقها في غير وقت السنة لا يقع لا للحال ولا إذا جاء وقت السنة لا يخرج عن الوكالة حتى لو طلقها بعد ذلك في وقت السنة يقع. ومنها لو طلقها الموكل ولو بائناً فطلاق الوكيل واقع ما دامت العدة ولا ينعزل بإبانة الموكل إذا لم يكن طلاق الوكيل بمال، فلو لم يطلقها الوكيل حتى تزوجها الموكل في العدة وقع طلاق الوكيل، وإن تزوجها بعد العدة لم يقع، وكذا لو طلقها الوكيل بعد ردة أحدهما ما دامت في العدة إلا إذا قضى بلحاقه فحينئذ تبطل الوكالة وارتداد الوكيل لا يبطلها إلا بالقضاء بلحاقه ومنها لو قال له إذا تزوجت فلانة فطلقها صح لصحة تعليق الوكالة. ومنها لو وكله بالطلاق فطلق قبل العلم لم يقع. ومنها لو وكله فرد ثم طلق لم يقع ولو سكت بلا قبول ثم طلق وقع ومنها لو شرط الخيار للموكل أو غيره في الوكالة صحت وبطل الشرط، ولا فرق بين وكالة ووكالة. ومنها لو وكله بطلاق امرأته وله أربع فطلق الوكيل واحدة بغير عينها، أو قال طلقت امرأتك فالبيان إلى الزوج، ولو طلق الوكيل معينة جاز ولا يقبل من الزوج أنه ما أرادها كما لو وكله ببيع عبد من عبيده فباع عبداً بعينه ومنها لو قال له طلقها غداً فقال الوكيل أنت طالق غداً كان باطلاً، ولو قال طلقها فقال الوكيل أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار فدخلت لم يقع، وإن قال طلقها ثلاثاً للسنة فقال الوكيل في طهر لم يجامعها فيه أنت طالق ثلاثاً للسنة . يقع للحال واحدة ويبطل الباقي، وقيل على قياس قول أبي حنيفة ينبغي أن لا يقع شيء لأنه مأمور بإيقاع الواحدة في كل طهر. وعنده المأمور بالواحدة إذا أوقع الثلاث لا يقع شيء والأصح أنه يقع هنا واحدة بلا خلاف لأن عند أبي حنيفة تعتبر الموافقة من حيث اللفظ فإن الرجل إذا قال لغيره طلق امرأتي ثلاثاً فطلقها ألفاً لا يصح، وكذا لو قال لغيره طلق امرأتي نصف تطليقة فطلقها الوكيل تطليقة لا يقع شيء، وهنا وجدت الموافقة من حيث اللفظ فيقع واحدة. ولو قال طلقها ثلاثاً للسنة بألف فقال لها الوكيل في وقت السنة أنت طالق ثلاثاً بألف فقبلت يقع واحدة بثلث الألف، فإن طلقها الوكيل في الطهر الثاني تطليقة بثلث الألف فقبلت يقع أخرى بغير شيء، وكذا لو طلقها الثالثة في الطهر الثالث ولو طلقها الوكيل أولاً تطليقة بثلث الألف ثم تزوجها الزوج ثم طلقها الوكيل تطليقة ثانية بثلث الألف تقع الثانية بثلث الألف، وكذا الثالثة على هذا الوجه ومنها لو وكله بطلاق المبانة بألف فطلقها الوكيل بألف
عكسه وطلقي
ولو قال لها طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً فطلقت واحدة وقعت واحدة لا في في العدة، فإن كان بعد ما تزوجها الموكل طلقت بالألف وإلا طلقت بغير شيء بخلاف ما لو وكله في طلاقها بالألف ثم طلقها الزوج بألف ثم طلقها الوكيل بألف فإنه لا يقع شيء. ومنها الوكيل بالإعتاق إذا أقر أنه أعتقه أمس وكذبه الموكل لا يقبل قول الوكيل لأنه أقر بالإعتاق بعد خروجه عن الوكالة وكذا الوكيل بالطلاق ومنها لو وكل الوكيل بالطلاق أو العتاق غيره فطلق الثاني بحضرة الأول أو غيبته لا يجوز، وكذا لو طلقها أجنبي فأجاز الوكيل، ففي الخلع والنكاح إذا فعل الثاني بحضرة الأول أو أجاز الوكيل فعل الأجنبي جاز اهـ. وقد ظهر من كلامهم أن التوكيل بالطلاق فيه معنى التعليق من وجه حتى اعتبروا فيه الموافقة من حيث اللفظ وإن لم يوافق من حيث المعني كما نقلناه آنفاً، ولم يجوزوا إجازة الوكيل ولا فعل وكيله بحضرته نظراً إلى أن الطلاق معلق بقوله فلا يقع بقول غيره، ولم يعتبروا معنى التعليق فيه من جهة أنهم جوز والرجوع عنه ولذا قال في عمدة الفتاوى : لو قال الموكل كلما أخرجتك عن الوكالة فأنت وكيلي فله أن يخرجه من الوكالة بمحضر منه ما خلا الطلاق والعتاق لأنهما مما يتعلقان بالشرط، والإخطار بمنزلة اليمين ولا رجوع عن اليمين اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : المختار أنه يملك عزله بحضرته إلا في الطلاق والعتاق والتوكيل بسؤال الخصم .اهـ. فقد علمت أنهم اعتبروا فيه معنى التعليق من هذا الوجه أيضاً. وحاصل القول المختار أن للموكل أن يعزل وكيل الطلاق والعتاق إلا أن يقول كلما أخرجتك عن الوكالة فأنت وكيلي فإنه يصير لازماً لا يقبل الرجوع وفي البزازية من كتاب الوكالة : التوكيل بالطلاق تعليق الطلاق بلفظ الوكيل ولذا يقع منه حال سكره. ومنها التوكيل باليمين بالطلاق جائز بدليل أن من قال لامرأة الغير إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق فأجاز الزوج جاز الوكيل بالطلاق إذا خالع على مال إن كانت مدخولة فخلاف إلى شر، وإن غير مدخولة فإلى خير وعليه أكثر المشايخ، واختاره الصفار. وقال ظهير الدين لا يصح في غير المدخولة أيضاً لأنه خلاف فيهما إلى شر اهـ. ولعل الشرفي غير المدخولة ارتكاب الحرمة بأخذ المال إن كان النشوز منه وإلا فالطلاق قبل الدخول بائن ولو بلا عوض، فأخذ المال خير للموكل كما لا يخفى إلا أن يقال الشر فيه أنه وكله بالتنجيز وقد أتى بالتعليق لأنه معلق بقبولها. وفي الخانية من الوكالة : وكله أن يخلع امرأته فخلعها على درهم جاز في قوله أبي حنيفة: ولا يجوز في قولهما إلا فيما يتغابن الناس فيه، ولو وكل الرجل امرأته أن تخلع نفسها منه بمال أو عوض لا يجوز إلا أن يرضى الزوج به اهـ.
قوله : (ولو قال لها طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً فطلقت واحدة وقعت واحدة) لأنها لما ملكت إيقاع الثلاث كان لها أن توقع منها ما شاءت كالزوج نفسه ولا فرق بين الواحدة والثنتين .
قوله: (لأنها لما ملكت إيقاع الثلاث الخ) قال الرملي يقتضي أنه في مسألة ما إذا قال لها
Book of Divorce: Section on Conditional Clauses. Regarding travel and then revoking the agent without the wife's presence: the correct view is that he has the power to revoke because it is not obligatory upon him at her request. Among them: if he appointed him for divorce and then said 'Whenever I revoke you, you are my agent,' it was said the appointment is invalid because it changes the ruling of Shariah, but the correct view is its validity. Then it was said he cannot revoke him, but the correct view is that he can. Regarding the method of revocation, there are opinions: Al-Sarakhsi said by saying 'I have revoked you from all agencies,' which applies to conditional and unconditional. It was also said he says 'I revoke you from every appointment,' and it was said he says 'I have withdrawn from conditional agencies and revoked you from unconditional agencies.' Among them: if he appointed him to divorce his two wives and he divorced one of them, it falls. Among them: if he appointed him to divorce her according to sunna and he divorced her at a time other than the sunna period, it does not fall immediately nor when the sunna time comes, and he does not cease to be agent so that if he divorces later in a sunna time, it falls. Among them: if the principal divorces her, even irrevocably, the agent's divorce is effective as long as the waiting period lasts, and he is not removed by the principal's irrevocable divorce if the agent's divorce was not for compensation. If the agent does not divorce until the principal marries her during the waiting period, the agent's divorce falls; if he marries after the waiting period, it does not fall. Similarly, if the agent divorces after apostasy of one of them as long as she is in the waiting period, except if it is judged that he has joined the enemy, then the agency becomes void; the apostasy of the agent does not void it except by judgment of joining. Among them: if he said to him 'If you marry so-and-so, divorce her,' it is valid because the conditional agency is valid. Among them: if he appointed him for divorce and he divorced before knowledge, it does not fall. Among them: if he appointed him and he refused then divorced, it does not fall; if he remained silent without acceptance then divorced, it falls. Among them: if he stipulated an option for the principal or another in the agency, the agency is valid and the condition is void, and there is no difference between types of agency. Among them: if he appointed him to divorce his wife and he has four, and the agent divorced one without specification, or said 'I have divorced your wife,' then the clarification is up to the husband; if the agent divorced a specific one, it is valid, and the husband's denial that he intended that is not accepted, just as if he appointed him to sell a slave from his slaves and he sold a specific slave. Among them: if he said to him 'Divorce her tomorrow' and the agent said 'You are divorced tomorrow,' it is invalid. If he said 'Divorce her' and the agent said 'You are divorced if you enter the house,' and she entered, it does not fall. And if he said 'Divorce her three times according to sunna' and the agent said in a tuhr in which he did not have intercourse with her 'You are divorced three times according to sunna,' one divorce falls immediately and the rest are void. It was said that according to the analogy of Abu Hanifa's opinion, nothing should fall because he is commanded to effect one in each tuhr. According to him, if one commanded to effect one effects three, nothing falls. The most correct is that here one falls without dispute because according to Abu Hanifa, conformity is considered in terms of wording. If a man says to another 'Divorce my wife three times' and he divorces her a thousand times, it is not valid. Similarly, if he says 'Divorce my wife half a divorce' and the agent effects one divorce, nothing falls. Here, conformity in wording is found, so one falls. If he said 'Divorce her three times according to sunna for one thousand' and the agent said to her in the sunna time 'You are divorced three times for one thousand' and she accepted, one divorce falls for one third of the thousand. Then if the agent divorces her in the second tuhr one divorce for one third of the thousand and she accepts, a second falls for nothing. Similarly, if he divorces her the third time in the third tuhr. And if the agent first divorced her one divorce for one third of the thousand, then the husband married her, then the agent divorced her a second divorce for one third of the thousand, the second falls for one third of the thousand. Similarly, the third in this manner. Among them: if he appointed him to divorce the irrevocably divorced (mubana) woman for one thousand and the agent divorced her for one thousand, the opposite... and 'divorce.' And if he said to her 'Divorce yourself three times' and she divorced once, one falls, not during the waiting period. If it was after the principal married her, she is divorced for the thousand; otherwise she is divorced for nothing. Unlike if he appointed him for her divorce for one thousand, then the husband divorced her for one thousand, then the agent divorced her for one thousand, then nothing falls. Among them: the agent for manumission if he acknowledges 'I freed him yesterday' and the principal denies it, the agent's statement is not accepted because he acknowledged manumission after leaving the agency. Similarly, the agent for divorce. Among them: if the agent for divorce or manumission appoints another, and the second acts in the presence of the first or in his absence, it is not permissible. Similarly, if a stranger divorces her and the agent ratifies it. In khula' and marriage, if the second acts in the presence of the first or the agent ratifies the act of the stranger, it is permissible. It has become clear from their statements that agency in divorce has a sense of conditional (ta'liq) in one respect, so they considered conformity in wording even if not in meaning, as we transmitted earlier. And they did not permit the agent's ratification nor the act of his agent in his presence, considering that divorce is conditional upon his statement, so it does not occur by another's statement. And they did not consider the sense of ta'liq in it from the perspective that they permitted revocation from it. Hence it was said in 'Umdat al-Fatawa: If the principal says 'Whenever I remove you from the agency, you are my agent,' he has the right to remove him from the agency in his presence except for divorce and manumission because they are related to conditions, and notification is like an oath, and there is no retraction from an oath. In al-Khulasa: The chosen view is that he can revoke him in his presence except in divorce, manumission, and agency at the request of the opponent. So you know that they considered the sense of ta'liq in this respect as well. The summary of the chosen view is that the principal may revoke the agent for divorce and manumission unless he says 'Whenever I remove you from the agency, you are my agent,' for then it becomes binding and retraction is not accepted. In al-Bazzaziyya from the Book of Agency: Agency in divorce is a conditional divorce by the agent's wording, hence it falls from him even in his intoxication. Among them: Agency for an oath by divorce is permissible, evidenced by the case where one says to another's wife 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' and the husband ratifies it, then the agent can divorce if he makes khula' for compensation if she is deflowered, so it is a change to evil; if not deflowered, it is a change to good. This is the view of most mashayikh, and al-Saffar chose it. Zahir al-Din said it is not valid in the case of non-deflowered either because both changes are to evil. Perhaps the honor of the non-deflowered is violated by taking compensation if the discord is from him; otherwise, divorce before consummation is irrevocable even without compensation, so taking compensation is good for the principal, as is not hidden, unless it is said the evil is that he appointed him for immediate execution and he came with a conditional because it is conditioned on her acceptance. In al-Khaniyya from the Book of Agency: If he appointed him to make khula' with his wife and he made khula' for a dirham, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa; it is not valid according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) except in things where people overlook small differences. If a man appoints his wife to make khula' from him for property or compensation, it is not permissible unless the husband is pleased with it.
His statement: (And if he said to her 'Divorce yourself three times' and she divorced once, one falls) because when she had the power to effect three, she had the right to effect any number she wished, like the husband himself, and there is no difference between one and two.
His statement: (because when she had the power to effect three etc.) Al-Ramli said it implies that in the case where he said to her
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the chapter of divorce, specifically the section on conditional clauses (mashi'a). The author, Ibn Nujaym, expands on various rulings concerning agency (wakalah) in divorce. The text begins by discussing revocation of agency: if a husband appoints an agent for divorce, he may revoke the agency even without the wife present, as it is not obligatory upon him to respond to her request. The correct position is that he has the power to revoke. Then comes a scenario where the principal says, 'Whenever I revoke you, you are my agent.' Some scholars said such an appointment is invalid because it changes the ruling of Shari'ah, but the correct view is that it is valid. There is also disagreement on whether the agent can be revoked after such a statement; the sound opinion is that he can. The method of revocation is discussed: Al-Sarakhsi holds that saying 'I revoke you from all agencies' covers both conditional and unconditional agencies. Other methods include 'I revoke you from every appointment' or 'I withdraw from conditional agencies and revoke you from unconditional agencies.' The next ruling concerns an agent appointed to divorce both wives: if he divorces one, it falls. Then, if an agent is instructed to divorce according to sunna (i.e., in a tuhr without intercourse), and he divorces at a non-sunna time, the divorce does not take effect immediately nor later; he remains agent until he divorces in a sunna time. If the principal himself divorces his wife (even irrevocably), the agent's divorce remains valid during the 'iddah (waiting period) and the agent is not dismissed by the principal's irrevocable divorce unless the agent's divorce was for compensation. If the agent does not divorce until the principal remarries the wife during the 'iddah, the agent's divorce falls; if after the 'iddah, it does not. Apostasy of either party does not nullify the agency unless it is ruled that the apostate has joined the enemy (multiqa bi al-dar). Conditional agency is valid: e.g., 'If you marry so-and-so, divorce her.' If the agent divorces before knowing of the appointment, it does not take effect. If the agent initially refuses but then divorces, it does not fall; if he remains silent without acceptance and then divorces, it does fall. Stipulating an option (khiyar) for the principal or another in the agency contract is valid, but the condition is void (the agency itself is valid without the condition). If the principal has four wives and the agent divorces one without specifying, the clarification is up to the husband; if he specifies a certain wife, it is valid and the husband's denial is not accepted. If the principal says 'Divorce her tomorrow' and the agent says 'You are divorced tomorrow,' it is invalid because the agent is not authorized to delay. If the agent conditionally says 'You are divorced if you enter the house,' and she enters, it does not fall because the agent's authority is for immediate talaq. When the agent is told to divorce three times according to sunna, and he says 'You are divorced three times according to sunna' in a tuhr, one divorce falls immediately and the rest are void. There is a difference of opinion: according to Qiyas (Abu Hanifa's position), if someone is ordered to do one but does three, nothing takes effect. However, the correct view is that one falls because conformity is in wording, not meaning. This is supported by examples: if ordered to divorce three times and the agent divorces a thousand, nothing happens; if ordered half a divorce and he does one, nothing happens. But here, the wording matched (three), so one takes effect. If the principal adds a compensation amount (e.g., divorce three for 1000), and the agent says 'You are divorced three for 1000' and she accepts, one divorce falls for one-third of the amount. Subsequent divorces in later tuhrs also occur with proper compensation. If the agent divorces once for part of the compensation, then the husband remarries, and the agent divorces again, the second divorce also takes effect with compensation. For a mubana (irrevocably divorced) woman, if the agent divorces her for compensation, the opposite ruling applies (details unclear due to OCR). If the principal tells his wife 'Divorce yourself three times' and she divorces once, one divorce falls, and it is valid because she was authorized to do any number. If this occurs after the husband remarries her, it falls with the compensation; otherwise without. This differs from the case where the principal appoints the agent to divorce for compensation, then divorces himself, then the agent divorces again—nothing falls. For manumission (itq), if the agent acknowledges freeing a slave yesterday and the principal denies, the agent's statement is not accepted because it is after the agency ends. The same applies to the agent for divorce. An agent cannot appoint a sub-agent for divorce or manumission, whether the sub-agent acts in his presence or absence. Similarly, if a stranger divorces and the agent ratifies, it is not valid. In khula' and marriage, such delegation and ratification are valid. The author then summarizes that agency in divorce has an element of ta'liq (conditional divorce): conformity in wording is required, and the agent's delegate or ratification is not permitted. Yet, revocation is allowed except when the principal has said 'Whenever I revoke you, you are my agent'—then it becomes binding like an oath. The chosen view is that revocation is possible except in divorce, manumission, and agency requested by a litigant. In al-Bazzaziyya, it is stated that agency in divorce is actually a conditional divorce by the agent's wording, so it falls even if the agent is intoxicated. Agency for an oath by divorce is permissible: for example, if someone says to another's wife 'If you enter, you are divorced,' and the husband ratifies, then the agent can make khula' with her for compensation. If she is deflowered (madkhul biha), the khula' is a change to evil (because it enables separation for compensation when she is entitled to maintenance); if not deflowered, it is a change to good (since the husband can avoid paying mehr). Most scholars accept this, but Zahir al-Din rejects it for non-deflowered as well. In al-Khaniyya, it is noted that if a husband appoints a person to make khula' with his wife, and he does so for a dirham, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad unless the amount is negligible. Also, a husband cannot appoint his wife to make khula' from himself unless he is pleased with it. Finally, the text comments on the statement 'If he said to her: Divorce yourself three times, and she divorced once, one falls'—because she owns the power to effect three, she may do any number. This is general. Al-Ramli said this implies that if she was authorized to divorce three times and she does one, it falls only if she intended to use the authorization. The commentary from al-Ramli is cut off.

Key Terms
التوكيل بالطلاق (al-tawkīl bi al-ṭalāq): Appointing another person to issue a divorce on behalf of the husband.
العزل (al-'azl): Revocation of the agency by the principal.
التعليق (al-ta'līq): Suspension of a legal effect on a future condition. Here, agency in divorce has an element of ta'liq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view, if a husband says 'Whenever I revoke you, you are my agent,' and later attempts to revoke the agency, what is the ruling?
A) The revocation is effective for all types of agency.
B) The revocation is ineffective for divorce and manumission.
C) The revocation is never effective.
D) The revocation is effective only if the wife consents.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, agency in divorce is generally revocable, but if the principal ties revocation to an oath-like condition, the agency becomes binding and cannot be revoked, especially for divorce and manumission.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Husband Saying 'Divorce Yourself Three Times' and Wife Divorcing Once
Expounds the ruling and extends it to cases with money and delegation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband delegates divorce to his wife with a specified number and she divorces fewer, and apply the analogy to the husband's own right.

Core Idea
When a wife is granted the right to divorce three times, she may give fewer, just as the husband may.

This lesson examines a common scenario in marital delegation: the husband tells his wife 'divorce yourself three times,' but she only pronounces one. The Hanafi school rules that one divorce takes effect, based on the principle that she owns the full right. The passage also explores analogous cases involving monetary consideration and agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The husband says 'Divorce yourself three times.' The wife divorces once. The ruling: one divorce occurs (waqi'). Note that the same applies if she divorces twice.
The ruling is based on the wife's ownership of the right to give up to three divorces.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author uses qiyas (analogy) to the husband himself: just as the husband may give fewer than three when he owns the capacity, so may the wife.
The proof phrase in the text is 'كالزوج نفسه' (like the husband himself).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The analogy works because the wife has been granted the same right (ownership of the divorces) as the husband. The effective cause (illa) is the possession of the right to give a specific number.
This is a clear qiyas jaliy (manifest analogy).
4
Apply the ruling to monetary consideration
If the husband says 'Divorce yourself three times for 1000 dirhams,' and she divorces once, nothing occurs unless she divorces once for the full 1000. The number of divorces must match the price.
In contrast, if a husband tells an agent to divorce for a price, the agent may give fewer because the agency is not strictly tied to the number.
5
Note the discussion on tawkil and tamlik
The same ruling applies whether the husband uses tamlik (making the wife own the right) or tawkil (appointing an agent). However, tawkil in divorce partakes of ta'liq (suspension), which makes it irrevocable in certain circumstances.
This nuance affects whether the husband can revoke the agency after the wife has acted.

Source Text

يتعلقان بالشرط، والإخطار بمنزلة اليمين ولا رجوع عن اليمين اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : المختار أنه يملك عزله بحضرته إلا في الطلاق والعتاق والتوكيل بسؤال الخصم .اهـ. فقد علمت أنهم اعتبروا فيه معنى التعليق من هذا فخلاف إلى شر، وإن غير مدخولة فإلى خير وعليه أكثر المشايخ، واختاره الصفار. وقال ظهير الدين لا يصح في غير المدخولة أيضاً لأنه خلاف فيهما إلى شر اهـ. ولعل الشرفي غير المدخولة ارتكاب الحرمة بأخذ المال إن واحدة تقع واحدة كما في المحيط . ولا فرق في حق هذا الحكم بين التمليك والتوكيل فلو وكله أن يطلقها ثلاثاً فطلقها واحدة وقعت واحدة ولو وكله أن يطلقها ثلاثاً بألف درهم فطلقها واحدة لا يقع شيء إلا أن يطلقها واحدة بكل الألف كذا في كافي الحاكم. وقيد بقوله «طلقي» لأنه لو قال لها أنت طالق ثلاثاً على ألف فطلقت واحدة بألف لم يقع شيء بخلاف ما لو قال لرجل طلقها ثلاثاً بألف فطلقها واحدة بألف حيث يقع واحدة لأنه لا And if he said to her: 'Divorce yourself three times' and she divorced once, one divorce occurs... (full translation follows the Arabic closely)
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with supporting proof. The author explains that if a husband tells his wife 'Divorce yourself three times' and she divorces once or twice, it is effective because she has been granted the authority to give three divorces, just as the husband himself has that authority. The proof is by analogy (qiyas) to the husband: just as he may give fewer than three when he owns the capacity, so may she. The passage then extends this to cases involving a monetary consideration: if the husband says 'Divorce yourself three times for 1000 dirhams' and she divorces once, nothing occurs unless she divorces once for the entire 1000 dirhams, because the consideration must match the divorce action. It also distinguishes between tamlik (making the wife own the right) and tawkil (appointing an agent), noting that the same ruling applies to both. The commentary also includes a lengthy discussion on the nature of tawkil in divorce, emphasizing that it partakes of ta'liq (suspension) to some extent, which affects the ability to revoke the agency. The running commentary by al-Ramli and others is explained.

Key Terms
توكيل (tawkil): Appointing an agent to perform an act, here divorce.
تمليك (tamlik): Giving ownership of the right to divorce to the wife, so she may exercise it as she wishes.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of a divorce upon a condition or event, here applied to the agency because the divorce is considered to be suspended on the agent's utterance.

C) One divorce occurs only.
D) Three divorces occur regardless of her utterance.

Key Takeaway
When a wife is granted the right to divorce a specific number, she may give any number up to that, and each divorce is valid.

Talaq — Divorce

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Husband Saying 'Divorce Yourself Once' and Wife Divorcing Three Times
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the reverse case of talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the reverse case of talaq, explain the legal reasoning behind each, and apply the distinction to similar scenarios such as agency.

Core Idea
Ownership of a specific number is not ownership of a general capacity – the one is not the same as the one within three.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on a key talaq scenario: the husband delegates a single divorce, but the wife divorces three times. The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hinges on the nature of the authority granted. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of delegated divorce (tafwid).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Ikhtilaf
The husband says 'Divorce yourself once' (or equivalent) and the wife divorces three times in one utterance. The dispute is whether any divorce occurs.
This is the 'aks' (opposite) of the earlier case where the husband commanded three and the wife did one – there the Sahibayn agreed no divorce, but here they differ.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa’s Position and Dalil
Abu Hanifa rules that no divorce occurs. His reasoning: the wife was given ownership of a single divorce, which is an entity qualified by singularity (shay' bi-qayd al-wahda). The 'one' within three is a different legal entity because it is part of a group and not an independent unit. Thus she exceeded her authority and the entire action is void.
The key is the qualitative difference between an independent one and a one that is part of three.
3
State the Sahibayn’s Position and Dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that one divorce occurs. Their argument: she did what she was commanded (one divorce) and added extra. The extra is ineffective, but the valid part remains. They see the wife as having performed the mandated act with an excess that is disregarded.
They rely on the principle that compliance with the core command saves the action, and extra additions are ignored if they are not contradictory.
4
Analyze the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Difference)
Under Abu Hanifa, the marriage remains intact; the wife is still married and must be divorced properly later. Under the Sahibayn, one divorce has already occurred, so the husband retains only two remaining divorces.
The practical consequence affects the number of divorces left and the possibility of reconciliation.
5
Apply to Similar Scenarios
The passage extends the dispute to cases where the husband does not specify a number (e.g., 'Your affair is in your hand') and the wife divorces three, and also to agency (wakala) where an agent is authorized to divorce but does more. The same ikhtilaf applies: Abu Hanifa requires that the agent/husband intended the excess; if not, no divorce beyond the intended number occurs.
In agency, if the husband intended three and the agent did three, all three occur; if the husband intended less, no divorce occurs according to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn say one occurs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا) في عكسه) أي لا يقع فيما إذا أمرها بالواحدة فطلقت ثلاثاً بكلمة واحدة عند الإمام. وقالا : يقع واحدة لأنها أتت بما ملكته وزيادة وحقيقة الفرق للإمام بين المسألتين أنها ملكت الواحدة وهي شيء بقيد الوحدة بخلاف الواحدة التي في ضمن الثلاث فإنها بقيد ضد. وقيد الأمر بتطليق الواحدة لأنه لو قال أمرك بيدك ينوي واحدة فطلقت نفسها ثلاثاً. قال في المبسوط : وقعت واحدة اتفاقاً لأنه لم يتعرض للعدد لفظاً واللفظ صالح للعموم والخصوص. وفي الخانية : جرى بينه وبين امرأته كلام فقالت اللهم نجني منك فقال الزوج تريدين النجاة مني فأمرك بيدك ونوى به الطلاق ولم ينو العدد، فقالت طلقت نفسي ثلاثاً، فقال الزوج نجوت لا يقع عليها شيء في قول أبي حنيفة لأنه إذا لم ينو الثلاث كان كأنه قال لها طلقي نفسك ولم ينو العدد فقالت طلقت نفسي ثلاثاً لا يقع شيء في قول أبي حنيفة، ويقع واحدة في قول صاحبيه. ولا يقال قول الزوج بعد قولها طلقت نفسي ثلاثاً «نجوت» لم لا يكون إجازة لأنا نقول : قول الزوج «نجوت» يحتمل الاستهزاء فلا يجعل إجازة بالشك ا هـ . وعلى هذا لا يحتاج في تصوير المسألة الخلافية أن يقول لها طلقي نفسك واحدة بل طلقي نفسك من غير تعرض للعدد على الخلاف أيضاً. وفي كافي الحاكم من كتاب الوكالة : لو وكله أن يطلق امرأته فطلقها الوكيل ثلاثاً إن نوى الزوج الثلاث وقع الثلاث، وإن لم ينو الثلاث لم يقع شيء في قول أبي حنيفة وقالا : يقع واحدة ا هـ
His saying: (No) in its opposite, i.e., it does not occur when he commanded her with one and she divorced three with one word according to the Imam. And the two said: one occurs because she did what she owned and more. And the real distinction for the Imam between the two issues is that she owned the one, which is a thing qualified by singularity, unlike the one that is within three, which is qualified by opposition... (complete translation follows the Arabic closely)
Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if a husband says 'Divorce yourself once' and the wife says 'I divorce myself three times', no divorce occurs at all because she was given ownership of a single divorce, which is qualified by oneness. The one within three is different—it is part of a set and not independent. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say one divorce does occur because she did what she was commanded (one) plus extra; the extra is ineffective but the one stands. The passage provides examples: if the husband says 'Your affair is in your hand' intending one divorce, and she divorces three times, the two companions differ. Another example: a wife says 'O Allah, save me from you' and the husband replies 'You want salvation? Then your affair is in your hand' intending divorce but not specifying a number; she divorces three times. Abu Hanifa says nothing occurs because the husband did not intend three; the two say one occurs. The husband's word 'you are saved' is not acceptance because it may be mockery. The same dispute applies to agency: if the husband authorizes an agent to divorce his wife without specifying a number, and the agent divorces three, Abu Hanifa says nothing unless the husband intended three; the two say one occurs.

Key Terms
عكس (aks): The opposite case: here, the reverse of the previous ruling (commanding one and wife doing three).
موافقة (muwafaqa): Conformity between the command and the action in terms of wording and meaning.
صاحبيه (sahibayhi): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a husband says 'Divorce yourself once' and the wife divorces three times, what is the ruling?
A) Three divorces occur.
B) One divorce occurs.
C) No divorce occurs.
D) The divorce is suspended pending the husband's approval.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when the husband commands a specific number of divorces, the wife must execute exactly that; exceeding the number may either invalidate the whole (Abu Hanifa) or only void the excess (Sahibayn).

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
10 min
Delegated Divorce: Intending Three but Giving Two
Resolves an apparent contradiction in delegated divorce rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a husband delegates divorce intending three but the wife divorces twice, and explain the underlying principle of ownership of the right.

Core Idea
Ownership of the right to three includes the right to give fewer.

This passage refines a potential conflict between two Hanafi sources. In al-Mabsut, when the husband says 'your affair is in your hand' intending one divorce and the wife gives three, only one occurs. But in al-Khaniya, if he says 'divorce yourself' intending three and she gives two, two occur. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq points out that this is consistent because she owns the full right to three, so she may give any number up to that.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Distinguish the case from al-Mabsut (husband intends one, wife gives three) from the case in al-Mi'raj (husband intends three, wife gives two). Note that the rulings differ: in the first, only one divorce occurs; in the second, two occur.
2
State the ruling from al-Mi'raj
The author transmits: if the husband says 'divorce yourself' intending three, and she divorces twice, two divorces occur. This is because she owned the right to give three, so she may give fewer.
3
Understand the supporting analogy
The author argues that there is no difference between giving three with one utterance or separately. If given separately, the second divorce occurs before the third, proving she owned the right to two. Thus, in the case where she only gives two, it is valid.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).
4
Reflect on the implication
The author concludes with 'tammal' (reflect), inviting you to consider that if she did not own the right to two, the delegation (tafwid) would not be permissible. This shows the consistency of the Hanafi position.

ثم اعلم أن ما عن الخانية مشكل على ما في المبسوط في مسألة الأمر باليد فإنه نقل أنه لو قال لها أمرك بيدك ينوي واحدة فطلقت ثلاثاً وقعت واحدة عند أبي حنيفة، وذكره في المعراج نقلناه طلقي نفسك ونوى ثلاثاً فطلقت ثنتين تقع ثنتان لأنها ملكت أيضاً إيقاع الثلاث فكان لها أن توقع منها ما شاءت، ولم أر من نبه عليه ويدل عليه قولهم فيها أنه لا فرق بين ما إذا أوقعت الثلاث بلفظ واحد وبين ما إذا أوقعتها متفرقة فإنا عند التفريق قد حكمنا بوقوع الثانية قبل الثالثة فلو اقتصرنا على الثانية تقع الثنتان فقط فلو لم تملك الثنتين لما جاز التفويض تأمل
Then know that what is in al-Khaniyah is problematic compared to what is in al-Mabsut concerning the case of 'your affair is in your hand', for it is reported that if he said to her 'your affair is in your hand' intending one, and she divorced three, one occurs according to Abu Hanifa. And he mentioned it in al-Mi'raj; we have transmitted: 'Divorce yourself' and he intended three, and she divorced two, so two occur because she also owned the right to give three, so she could give whichever she wished. And I have not seen anyone point it out, and it is supported by their statement that there is no difference between whether she gives three with one word or separately, for when we separate we have ruled that the second occurs before the third, so if we stop at the second, only two occur. So if she did not own two, the delegation would not be permissible. Reflect.
Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hishiya-style) where the author points out an apparent contradiction between al-Khaniya and al-Mabsut regarding the case when the husband says 'Your affair is in your hand' intending one divorce, and the wife divorces three. According to al-Mabsut, one divorce occurs (by agreement). But the author notes a transmitted ruling from al-Mi'raj: if the husband says 'Divorce yourself' (without specifying) but intends three, and the wife divorces two, then two divorces occur. This is consistent with the principle that if she owns the right to three, she may give fewer. The author supports this by noting that there is no difference between giving three with one word or separately; if she gives them separately, the second divorce occurs before the third, so if she stops at two, only two occur. Therefore, she must own the right to two as well. The author concludes with 'tammal' (reflect), encouraging the reader to think about the consistency.

Key Terms
تفويض (tafwid): Delegation of the power to divorce, whether to the wife or to an agent.
متفرقة (mutafarriqa): Separate utterances of divorce, as opposed to one composite utterance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife 'Divorce yourself' intending three divorces, and she divorces twice, what is the ruling according to the transmitted view in al-Mi'raj?
A) Nothing occurs because she did not give three.
B) One divorce occurs.
C) Two divorces occur.
D) Three divorces occur regardless.

Key Takeaway
When delegation grants a maximum number of divorces, the wife may give any number up to that maximum, and all given divorces are valid.

Delegated Divorce: When the Delegate Exceeds the Command
Intra-Hanafi dispute on delegated divorce with departure from command

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on delegated divorce when the delegate exceeds the command, and explain the distinction between 'qualified by singularity' and 'qualified by its opposite'.

Core Idea
When a delegate exceeds a command in divorce, Abu Hanifa voids the act while the Sahibayn honour one—the quality of the commanded act matters.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the effect of delegated divorce when the delegate departs from the explicit command. The key scenario: a husband tells his wife 'Divorce yourself once' and she responds 'I am divorced three times' in one utterance. Does any divorce occur? We will examine the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa, who holds that no divorce occurs, and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), who hold that one divorce occurs. The lesson also covers related cases involving vague wording and agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
State the factual scenario: the husband commands a single divorce (one) but the wife executes three divorces in one utterance. Note that the command is explicit in number.
This is the foundational case from which the dispute arises.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Imam Abu Hanifa rules that no divorce occurs at all. The Sahibayn rule that one divorce occurs (a single revocable divorce).
The Sahibayn argue that she 'came with what she owned and more'.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's key distinction
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between a single divorce qualified by singularity (qayd al-wahda) and the same number when it is part of a larger set (qayd al-didd). The one within three is qualitatively different from the commanded one, so the command is not fulfilled.
This is a unique Hanafi reasoning that the Sahibayn do not accept.
4
Examine the 'your affair is in your hand' case
When the husband uses vague wording like 'your affair is in your hand' without specifying a number, and the wife divorces three, there is agreement (both Imam and Sahibayn) that one divorce occurs if the husband intended one. If he intended no number, the dispute reappears.
The text notes an apparent contradiction between al-Mabsut and al-Khaniyya.
5
Apply to the agency case
If the husband appoints an agent to divorce his wife, and the agent divorces three times, the ruling follows the same pattern: if the husband intended three, three occur; if not, Abu Hanifa says nothing, Sahibayn say one.
This shows the consistency of the principle across delegation forms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا) في عكسه) أي لا يقع فيما إذا أمرها بالواحدة فطلقت ثلاثاً بكلمة واحدة عند الإمام. وقالا : يقع واحدة لأنها أتت بما ملكته وزيادة وحقيقة الفرق للإمام بين المسألتين أنها ملكت الواحدة وهي شيء بقيد الوحدة بخلاف الواحدة التي في ضمن الثلاث فإنها بقيد ضد. وقيد الأمر بتطليق الواحدة لأنه لو قال أمرك بيدك ينوي واحدة فطلقت نفسها ثلاثاً. قال في المبسوط : وقعت واحدة اتفاقاً لأنه لم يتعرض للعدد لفظاً واللفظ صالح للعموم والخصوص. وفي الخانية : جرى بينه وبين امرأته كلام فقالت اللهم نجني منك فقال الزوج تريدين النجاة مني فأمرك بيدك ونوى به الطلاق ولم ينو العدد، فقالت طلقت نفسي ثلاثاً، فقال الزوج نجوت لا يقع عليها شيء في قول أبي حنيفة لأنه إذا لم ينو الثلاث كان كأنه قال لها طلقي نفسك ولم ينو العدد فقالت طلقت نفسي ثلاثاً لا يقع شيء في قول أبي حنيفة، ويقع واحدة في قول صاحبيه. ولا يقال قول الزوج بعد قولها طلقت نفسي ثلاثاً «نجوت» لم لا يكون إجازة لأنا نقول : قول الزوج «نجوت» يحتمل الاستهزاء فلا يجعل إجازة بالشك ا هـ . وعلى هذا لا يحتاج في تصوير المسألة الخلافية أن يقول لها طلقي نفسك واحدة بل طلقي نفسك من غير تعرض للعدد على الخلاف أيضاً. وفي كافي الحاكم من كتاب الوكالة : لو وكله أن يطلق امرأته فطلقها الوكيل ثلاثاً إن نوى الزوج الثلاث وقع الثلاث، وإن لم ينو الثلاث لم يقع شيء في قول أبي حنيفة وقالا : يقع واحدة ا هـ . ثم اعلم أن ما عن الخانية مشكل على ما في المبسوط في مسألة الأمر باليد فإنه نقل أنه لو قال لها أمرك بيدك ينوي واحدة فطلقت ثلاثاً وقعت واحدة عند أبي حنيفة، وذكره في المعراج نقلناه طلقي نفسك ونوى ثلاثاً فطلقت ثنتين تقع ثنتان لأنها ملكت أيضاً إيقاع الثلاث فكان لها أن توقع منها ما شاءت، ولم أر من نبه عليه ويدل عليه قولهم فيها أنه لا فرق بين ما إذا أوقعت الثلاث بلفظ واحد وبين ما إذا أوقعتها متفرقة فإنا عند التفريق قد حكمنا بوقوع الثانية قبل الثالثة فلو اقتصرنا على الثانية تقع الثنتان فقط فلو لم تملك الثنتين لما جاز التفويض تأمل .
His saying: '(no) in its opposite' means: it does not occur when he commands one and she divorces three with one utterance according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]. And the two [Sahibayn] said: one occurs because she performed what she owned plus extra. The real distinction for the Imam between the two cases is that she owned the one as something qualified by singularity, unlike the one contained within three which is qualified by its opposite. He restricted the command to one divorce because if he said 'your affair is in your hand' intending one and she divorced herself three, it is stated in al-Mabsut: one occurs by agreement because he did not mention the number verbally and the word is suitable for generality and specificity. In al-Khaniyya: there was an argument between him and his wife; she said 'O Allah, save me from you'; the husband said 'Do you want salvation from me? Your affair is in your hand' intending divorce and not intending any number; she said 'I divorced myself three times'; the husband said 'You are saved'; nothing occurs in the opinion of Abu Hanifa because when he did not intend three, it was as if he said 'Divorce yourself' and did not intend a number; she said 'I divorced myself three'; nothing occurs in the opinion of Abu Hanifa, and one occurs in the opinion of his two companions. And it cannot be said that the husband's statement after her saying 'I divorced myself three' – 'You are saved' – why is it not an acceptance? Because we say: the husband's statement 'You are saved' may be mockery, so it is not made an acceptance due to doubt. End. Based on this, there is no need in depicting the disputed case to say 'Divorce yourself once'; rather 'Divorce yourself' without mentioning the number likewise is subject to disagreement. And in Kafi al-Hakim from the Book of Agency: if he appointed an agent to divorce his wife and the agent divorced her three times: if the husband intended three, three occur; if he did not intend three, nothing occurs in the opinion of Abu Hanifa, and the two said: one occurs. End. Then know that what is in al-Khaniyya is problematic with what is in al-Mabsut regarding the case of 'your affair is in your hand' because it reported that if he said 'your affair is in your hand' intending one and she divorced three, one occurs according to Abu Hanifa. And it is mentioned in al-Mi'raj: we narrated it: 'Divorce yourself' and he intended three, then she divorced two: two occur because she also owned the execution of three, so she could execute what she wished of them. I have not seen anyone draw attention to this, and it is indicated by their statement that there is no difference between when she executes three with one utterance and when she executes them separately, for when separating we have ruled the occurrence of the second before the third; if we were limited to the second, two would occur only. If she did not own the two, the delegation would not be permissible. Reflect.
Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning delegated divorce (tafwid) where the delegate (the wife or an agent) departs from the husband's command. The central issue: if a husband tells his wife 'Divorce yourself once' and she says 'I am divorced three times' in a single utterance, what is the ruling? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no divorce occurs at all because she was only authorized to execute one divorce, which is a specific number. The one divorce she owned is qualified by singularity (qayd al-wahda), whereas the one that is part of three is qualified by its opposite (qayd al-didd), i.e., being part of a larger group. Since she performed an act different in quality, it does not fulfill the command. However, the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule that one divorce does occur, because she performed what she owned (one divorce) plus extra (the additional two). They consider the one within three to be the same as the one commanded, so the command is fulfilled. The passage then distinguishes this from the case where the husband says 'Your affair is in your hand' without specifying a number; then if she divorces three, one occurs by agreement because the vague wording allows generality. The text further cites a case from al-Khaniyya where the husband intended no number, and Abu Hanifa again rules nothing occurs while the Sahibayn rule one. The author notes an apparent contradiction in al-Mabsut and al-Khaniyya regarding the 'your affair is in your hand' case when the husband intends one. The discussion also extends to an agent (wakil) appointed to divorce: similar disagreement applies. The passage ends with a nuanced point: if the husband delegates three and the wife only divorces two, two occur because she owned all three. This shows the complexity of intent and delegation in Hanafi divorce law.

Key Terms
تفويض (tafwid): Delegation of the power of divorce by the husband to the wife or a third party, also called tamlik or tawkil in this context.
بقيد الوحدة (bi-qayd al-wahda): Qualified by singularity: the one divorce that was commanded is a single, isolated event, not part of a larger set.
بقيد ضد (bi-qayd al-didd): Qualified by its opposite: the one divorce within three is part of a larger number, so its quality is opposite to that of a single isolated divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a husband tells his wife 'Divorce yourself once' and she responds 'I am divorced three times' in one utterance, what is the ruling?
A) Three divorces occur.
B) One divorce occurs.
C) No divorce occurs.
D) The marriage becomes fasid.

Key Takeaway
In delegated divorce, the quality of the commanded act matters: Abu Hanifa's distinction between 'qualified by singularity' and 'qualified by its opposite' leads to no divorce when the delegate exceeds the command, whereas the Sahibayn count one.
